"},{"id":31598,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/jason-kidd-10-things-know","date":"2019-10-02","title":"Jason Kidd: 10 things to know","content":"From his days as a high school legend in Oakland to 19 impressive NBA seasons, Jason Kidd was \u2018the first LeBron,\u2019 a guard who could do it all and presented opponents with a matchup nightmare. Here are 10 things to know about the Hall of Famer and one of the greatest point guards ever to play the game. * * * Point God: Kidd is one of the most unique point guards in NBA history. He ranks second in both assists and steals and has the most rebounds ever by a guard. What separates him from others at the position is his deference when it comes to shooting and scoring. Kidd averaged only 12.6 points in his 19-year career, made just 4.5 shots per game and his field-goal percentage sits at a rather underwhelming 40 percent. However, Kidd has the third-longest consecutive playoff streak in NBA history at 17 seasons, trailing only Karl Malone and John Stockton, and single-handedly turned around franchises when he arrived. In short, Kidd managed to win games in spite of his reluctance to score. Richard Jefferson, one of his teammates with the Nets, said: \u201cI don\u2019t think in the history of the game there has ever been a guy to dominate more games without scoring.\u201d Jumper in progress: The quip among NBA people about Kidd in college is that he had an NBA body and a YMCA jump shot. And for the most part of his 19 seasons, that was true. Kidd was one of the best passers in basketball history (college and pro) but shooting was problematic. Yet late in his career, he developed a dependable jumper from decent range and even became a threat from deep. Kidd shot nearly 36 percent from 3-point range after he turned 30 and was even a volume 3-point shooter with the Mavericks, taking nearly five per game. Kidd now ranks 10th in NBA history on the list of 3-pointers made (1,988). \u201cHe went from a non shooter when he first entered the league to a tremendous three-point shooter,\u201d said Rod Thorn, the former Nets executive who traded for Kidd. Prep power: Kidd was a legend in high school and this was well before YouTube and the Internet. He was already 6-foot-4 and threw entertaining passes that sometimes bounced off the hands of unsuspecting teammates. Gary Payton, another Oakland legend, compared him to Joe Montana with a basketball and said Kidd was \u201cthe first LeBron\u201d in terms of generating buzz in high school. Payton personally \u201ctrained\u201d Kidd in summer pickup games and the Glove, five years older, was relentless in his critiques and defensive efforts against Kidd, who complained to his parents that Payton \u201cwouldn\u2019t let me score.\u201d The tough-love helped because Kidd led his high school to consecutive state titles and won national player of the year as a senior. St. Joseph\u2019s, a small Catholic school (600 students) in Alameda, had to move some of its home games to the Oakland Coliseum because the demand to watch Kidd was intense; his games drew 12,000 at the Coliseum, often outselling the Warriors. The school also sold Jason Kidd T-shirts for $10 each to benefit its athletic program and the shirts sold briskly. Double Dallas: Kidd had two stints with the Mavericks, the first when he began his NBA career and the second when his career was winding down. The Mavericks in 1994-95 were rebuilding with youth, namely Kidd, Jamal Mashburn and Jim Jackson, while the Mavericks of 2011 were loaded with such veterans as Dirk Nowitzki, Tyson Chandler and Jason Terry. Kidd was traded after his first three seasons in Dallas to Phoenix partly because of an inability to mesh with Jackson and Mashburn; his immaturity was cited. Ironically, the Mavericks craved Kidd in 2008 because of his maturity; by then, Kidd had a string of successful seasons with the Nets where he showed great leadership skills with an otherwise average team. Turnaround man: When Kidd was traded by the Suns to the Nets in 2001, he inherited a wayward franchise coming off a last-place finish in the Atlantic Division. Kidd\u2019s impact was immediate and the Nets had a 26-game improvement, still tied for the sixth-biggest turnaround in NBA history with the 2003-04 Nuggets with rookie Carmelo Anthony. The top-five in that category are the 1997-98 Spurs (36 wins) helped by Tim Duncan\u2019s addition, the David Robinson Spurs of 1989-90 (35), the Celtics of 1979-80 (32) with Larry Bird, the Kareem Abdul-Jabbar Bucks of 1969-70 (29 wins) and the 1988-89 Suns (27) and Kevin Johnson. Kidd improved the Mavericks (23 wins), Suns (16 wins) and Nets in his first seasons with those teams. Spurned the Spurs: In the summer of 2003, right after he took the Nets to the NBA Finals for the second time in as many years but came up short of a title, Kidd became an unrestricted free agent at age 30. And one of the teams that made him a high priority was the Spurs, coached by Gregg Popovich and who then had a 27-year-old Tim Duncan, Manu Ginobili and a point guard they drafted two years earlier named Tony Parker. Popovich felt Parker, while promising, lacked the seasoning and leadership of Kidd. Putting Kidd next to Duncan, Popovich felt, would potentially form a dynasty; Kidd had finished second to Duncan in the 2001 MVP voting. The Spurs flew Kidd and his wife Joumana to San Antonio, where they were met by the recently-retired David Robinson. However, within days after Kidd returned to New Jersey , he signed a six-year, $99 million deal to stay with the Nets. The reason? His wife, who dabbled in TV, wanted to stay in the New York area to further her career. The couple divorced four years later, Parker led the Spurs to three more titles and won the 2007 Finals MVP, Kidd and the Nets never made it past the second round again and he didn\u2019t win his first NBA title until 2011 with the Mavericks. Trade quirk: The trade that sent Kidd from the Nets to the Mavericks was actually done on the second attempt. The first try fizzled when one of the players involved in the deal, Devean George, invoked his early Bird Rights and couldn\u2019t be included. So the redone trade was made when Keith Van Horn, the former Nets forward who had retired, came out of retirement just to be included in the package to make the salaries work. Van Horn received $4.3 million for the trouble of filing paperwork twice \u2014 to un-retire, get traded, then retire again. Champion finally: In his third NBA Finals, Kidd finally struck gold, helping the Mavericks beat Miami in 2011 . In that championship run throughout the postseason, Kidd averaged 9 points, 7.3 assists, 4.5 rebounds and nearly two steals per game. But while the numbers were relatively mild, he did leave a historic mark: At 38, Kidd became the oldest starting point guard ever to lead his team to a championship. Tie game: The co-winners of the 1995 Rookie of the Year award were Kidd and Grant Hill. Their careers then took separate roads: Hill had the better start while Kidd the more productive finish. Hill in his first five seasons, all with the Pistons, averaged 22 points, seven rebounds and six assists. Then he struggled the rest of his career while mending from ankle surgery; Hill went seven straight years without playing a full 82 games (and missed an entire season) until he hit that mark with the Suns in 2008-09. Kidd, meanwhile, was on his third team when he arrived in New Jersey in 2001, but soon finished just behind Tim Duncan for the MVP award and led the Nets to a pair of Finals appearances. Both Hill and Kidd retired in June of 2013; Hill announced his retirement two days before Kidd. New coach: Just nine days after retiring as a player, Kidd was named coach of the Nets , now relocated to Brooklyn. It was only the third time in NBA history that a player became a head coach the season after retiring, joining Mike Dunleavy (Lakers) and Paul Silas (Rockets). The Nets wanted Phil Jackson but he declined. Kidd interviewed with GM Billy King, who said of Kidd: \u201cHe reminded me of Larry Brown\u201d and was hired after a strong recommendation by Mike Krzyzewski, who coached Kidd on Team USA. The reunion was highlighted by the Nets retiring Kidd\u2019s No. 5; Kidd played seven seasons with the franchise, reached a pair of Finals, was an All-Star in five and first team All-NBA in two. He owns the only retired NBA jersey by the Nets; the rest are from the ABA."},{"id":31601,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/wizards-hire-rod-thorn-adviser","date":"2019-10-01","title":"Wizards hire ex-NBA executive Rod Thorn as adviser","content":" WASHINGTON (AP) \u2014 Former NBA GM and league executive Rod Thorn has been hired by the Washington Wizards as a senior adviser to general manager Tommy Sheppard. "},{"id":31578,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/nba-works-tighten-traveling-calls-2019-20","date":"2019-10-01","title":"NBA working to dispel misconceptions on traveling calls","content":" NEW YORK (AP) \u2014 James Harden slides sideways or steps backward, and the screaming starts. Whether seated on the opposing bench or on a stool in a sports bar, somebody is insisting that Harden must have traveled between the time he finished dribbling and launched his shot from a different spot. Traveling will be an emphasis this season for officials, who are determined not to allow offensive players to gain an extra edge by taking an extra step. Scoring stars like Harden already got an advantage once hand-checking on the perimeter was no longer legal, so they can\u2019t be given another one. \u201cIf we can\u2019t allow people to hand check, we can\u2019t allow them to travel because then they\u2019re almost unguardable,\u201d vice president of referee operations Mark Wunderlich said. That said, most times when Harden does his signature step-back, he doesn\u2019t travel. \u201cIt is legal, except for the fact that he gets a third step in every now and then when his rhythm is just off, which shows you the highlight of how difficult it is,\u201d said Monty McCutchen, the NBA\u2019s head of referee development and training. That\u2019s why referees are working harder to get it right. Critics of the NBA \u2014 and even some fans \u2014 have long sneered that the league doesn\u2019t call traveling. McCutchen said data showed officials were missing about two per game, but the way the game is played today can make those misses more penal for the defense. Players are bigger, faster and more skilled, and even big men who would have been centers in a previous generation are now do-everything forwards like 6-foot-11 Kia MVP Giannis Antetokounmpo. He already gets far enough with the two steps that are legal, forget when allowed a third. McCutchen compared the difference with Tiny Archibald, a 6-foot-1 guard who played in the 1970s and \u201980s. \u201cHe covered 10 feet with his two steps,\u201d McCutchen said. \u201cHow far is Giannis covering? The game has changed.\u201d So officials have begun to change with it, altering the way they were taught to officiate when McCutchen and Wunderlich were on the floor. Before, referees were trained to look first at the defensive player. Now they have reversed their sequencing, looking first at the offensive player\u2019s feet to make certain a legal pivot foot has been established and not changed. And the league added new language in the rule book to define the \u201cgather,\u201d to clarify how many steps a player can take after receiving the ball or completing his dribble. At the referees\u2019 preseason meetings and training camp last week, McCutchen said officials studied replays of three travels each time they returned from a break, and had a dedicated 45-minute session on traveling. An educational video was sent to teams , and the referees visited the coaches\u2019 preseason meetings, where they had a traveling station with two players on the floor so they could do demonstrations for the coaches. And Houston coach Mike D\u2019Antoni said the league stressed that Harden\u2019s step-back jumper is legal. \u201cThey made a point, which is great, to tell every head coach that is not traveling. It\u2019s not traveling,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said. \u201cSo hopefully coaches will quit complaining and hopefully you guys in the news will understand that that\u2019s not traveling. There\u2019s other points that we have to clean up that are traveling and the NBA is going to try to do a better job of that.\u201d San Antonio coach Gregg Popovich quipped last year that the step-back 3 came when players \u201cjump backwards and travel and shoot a 3.\u201d But the leaders of the referee team praised Harden for his cleverness and creativity. \u201cOn the dribble, we always talk about dribbling you can take two legal steps to the basket, right? No one ever thought about on the gather after you dribble you can take two legal steps backwards,\u201d Wunderlich said. Added Jason Phillips, who will oversee the Replay Center: \u201cThe rulebook doesn\u2019t state that the two steps have to be in any direction.\u201d Harden said it never should have been a debate, because if he was traveling then referees would have been whistling him for it. \u201cI\u2019m tired of hearing that\u2019s a travel, from coaches, from other players, from haters, fans, whatever you want to call it,\u201d Harden said. But he acknowledges it looks awkward, so the referees know they have to educate teams and fans just as much as themselves. There is no new rule or even a new interpretation of traveling, just a desire to correctly call the travels that are in the books. That\u2019s why it\u2019s the biggest emphasis on the preseason list of points of education. \u201cThe first one is traveling and the second one is traveling and the third, fourth and fifth one are traveling,\u201d McCutchen said. \u201cI\u2019m only joking to show that there are POEs and then there are POEs. We really want to get better at our fundamentals of the game and traveling is a big part of that.\u201d AP Sports Writer Kristie Rieken in Houston contributed to this report."},{"id":31580,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/chris-paul-happy-be-back-oklahoma-city","date":"2019-10-01","title":"Chris Paul excited about second stint in Oklahoma City","content":" OKLAHOMA CITY (AP) \u2014 Chris Paul is happy to be back where his professional career began. It\u2019s just been a great character builder and great to see the game from a different perspective.\u201d"},{"id":31661,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/college-athletes-endorsement-deals-lebron-james","date":"2019-10-01","title":"California to allow NCAA athletes to make money","content":"SACRAMENTO, Calif. (AP) \u2014 Defying the NCAA, California opened the way Monday for college athletes to hire agents and make money from endorsement deals with sneaker companies, soft drink makers, car dealerships and other sponsors, just like the pros. The first-in-the-nation law, signed by Democratic Gov. Gavin Newsom and set to take effect in 2023, could upend amateur sports in the U.S. and trigger a legal challenge. Newsom and others cast it as an attempt to bring more fairness to big-money college athletics and let players share in the wealth they create for their schools. Critics have long complained that universities are getting rich off the backs of athletes \u2014 often, black athletes struggling to get by financially. \u201cOther college students with a talent, whether it be literature, music, or technological innovation, can monetize their skill and hard work,\u201d the governor said. \u201cStudent athletes, however, are prohibited from being compensated while their respective colleges and universities make millions, often at great risk to athletes\u2019 health, academics and professional careers.\u201d Newsom predicted other states will introduce similar legislation. The NCAA \u2014 which had called on him to veto the bill, arguing that it would destroy the distinction between amateurs and pros and give California an unfair recruiting advantage \u2014 said it is considering its next steps. It did not elaborate. In a statement, the NCAA said it is working to revise its rules on making money off a player\u2019s name and likeness. But it said any changes should be made at the national level through the NCAA, not through a patchwork of state laws. California\u2019s law applies to students at both public and private institutions \u2014 but not community colleges \u2014 in the nation\u2019s most populous state. While the measure covers all sports, the big money is in football and basketball. Student athletes won\u2019t get salaries. But under the law, they can\u2019t be stripped of their scholarships or kicked off the team if they sign endorsement deals. There are some limitations: Athletes can\u2019t enter into deals that conflict with their schools\u2019 existing contracts. For example, if your university has a contract with Nike, you can\u2019t sign with Under Armour. The law represents another instance of California jumping out in front of other states when it comes to social and political change. The movement to allow student athletes to profit from their labors on the court or the playing field has been simmering for years, portrayed as a matter of economic fairness and civil rights. \u201cA majority of these athletes, it\u2019s no secret, are African American,\u201d said Sen. Steven Bradford, a co-author of the bill who is black. \u201cIt\u2019s an issue of fairness, and it\u2019s an issue that has been long overdue.\u201d Newsom tweeted a video showing him signing the law during a special episode of HBO\u2019s \u201cThe Shop: Uninterrupted\u201d alongside NBA superstar LeBron James, one of many professional athletes who have endorsed the measure. James, whose 14-year-old son is a closely watched basketball prospect in Los Angeles and will be 18 when the law takes effect, exulted over its signing on Instagram, saying it will \u201cchange the lives for countless athletes who deserve it!\u201d He added: \u201cNCAA, you got the next move. We can solve this for everyone!\u201d NBA rookie Jordan Poole of the Golden State Warriors also welcomed the new law. Six months ago, as a player at the University of Michigan, he hit a game-winning shot at the buzzer in the second round of the NCAA tournament as millions watched on TV. \u201cI know for sure I would have been using my name after that Houston shot,\u201d he said. His teammate, three-time NBA champion Draymond Green, went further. \u201cThe NCAA is a dictatorship,\u201d the former Michigan State star told reporters Monday. \u201cI\u2019m tired of seeing people get ripped off, and I\u2019m tired of seeing these college athletes being ripped off.\u201d Before the governor signed the law, the NCAA threatened to bar California universities from competition, meaning powerhouses such as the University of Southern California, UCLA, Stanford and the University of California, Berkeley, could find themselves banned. If that were to happen, California schools could form a new governing body and get schools from like-minded states to join, in a threat to the NCAA\u2019s dominance. But the governor, a former college baseball player, said he doubts the NCAA would kick California schools out, arguing that the state\u2019s 40 million people and status as the world\u2019s fifth-largest economy make it too big to lose. The NCAA \u201ccan\u2019t afford to do that,\u201d he said. Democratic state Sen. Nancy Skinner, the bill\u2019s author, said it could especially help female athletes, who have limited opportunities for professional sports once they leave college. \u201cCollege is the primary time when the spotlight is on\u201d them, Skinner said. \u201cFor women, this might be the only time they could make any money.\u201d NCAA rules bar players from hiring agents. The NCAA has also steadfastly refused to pay players in most cases. But a committee is studying other ways players could make money. Its report is expected in October. The NCAA does let some athletes accept money in some instances. Tennis players can accept up to $10,000 in prize money per year, and Olympians can accept winnings from their competitions. Also, many schools pay players yearly cost-of-living stipends of $2,000 to $4,000. \u201cWe just kind of joked every kid is going to want to go to college out here in Cali now,\u201d Warriors forward Glenn Robinson III, who played college ball at Michigan, said of the new law. \u201cI think it\u2019s time. A lot of people are waking up and starting to see how much money that these universities are making off of players,\u201d he added. \u201cWhere I went to school, a lot of players couldn\u2019t afford lunch. * * * AP sports writer Janie McCauley contributed reporting from San Francisco."},{"id":31653,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/media-day-behind-scenes-2019","date":"2019-10-01","title":"Media Day 2019: Behind the scenes with NBA teams","content":" As Monday drew to a close, every team had completed their media day festivities for the 2019-20 season. With a swell of attention now being paid to presumptive title favorites, who added Paul George and Kawhi Leonard while retaining much of the supporting cast, Beverley was given the chance Sunday to double down on his prophecy. He toned it down. \u201cWe\u2019ll see,\u201d he said. Yet his sinister grin was plain to see, and it reflected the swagger and internal expectations of a franchise not known for through-the-roof projections. Such is the new world order in Los Angeles, and perhaps the NBA, in 2019-20. These are unprecedented times for the Clippers, who\u2019ve had winning teams before but none with this much title twinkle headed into the season. \u201cWe know what we\u2019re capable of doing,\u201d said Beverley, and so does everyone else. You don\u2019t add the reigning NBA Finals MVP and another who finished third in the regular-season Kia MVP balloting without shaking up the establishment, even if you\u2019ve never won a championship in franchise history. But there\u2019s a long wait between now and next spring\u2019s playoffs, and a shorter one to see George on the floor.  The 29-year-old swingman is still in the mending stage after off-season surgery on both shoulders. He said \u201cI\u2019m not sure\u201d when he\u2019ll be ready to play, even with opening night against the Lakers a little over three weeks away. George said he hasn\u2019t had any complications or setbacks, but won\u2019t engage in any contact work in camp and coach Doc Rivers said George will not appear in any games until he does. \u201cThere\u2019s no problems,\u201d George said. \u201cI\u2019m just going to do light work and drills for now.\u201d The other issue as it relates to health is Leonard\u2019s usage. Last year in Toronto, still smarting from a persistent quad injury that led to his stormy exit from the Spurs, Leonard didn\u2019t play on consecutive nights during back-to-back games. Rivers said there are no such restrictions this season, or demands from the player, although the coach wants to reserve the right to monitor and change the approach if necessary. \u201cLast year, I was going in with an injury that I was dealing with the year before, still was lingering, and we knew that I had to be healthy going throughout the season and making it to the playoffs,\u201d Leonard said. \u201cThis time, I\u2019m feeling good. I\u2019m feeling way better than I was at the start of last season. There really was no plan laid out to discuss with everyone.\u201d Rivers also noted that the Clippers\u2019 depth will allow for rest periods for George and Leonard; both players are joining a team that prospered without an All-Star last season, a team that will probably once again bring reigning Sixth Man of the Year Lou Williams and Montrezl Harrell off the bench. In due time, the Clippers will be complete, and that\u2019s the most important takeaway from their first official gathering. The level of enthusiasm is \u201csky-high,\u201d said Williams. Rivers has flexibility with Leonard and George, widely considered among the most elite two-way players in basketball. On offense, George and Leonard are top-10 league scorers (26.6 points last year for Leonard; 28.0 for George). Playing those two alongside Williams, who averaged 20 points last season in just 26 minutes off the bench, should cause matchup headaches. \u201cWe\u2019ll force a lot of defenses to make a lot of hard decisions,\u201d said Williams. And the options afforded to Rivers might even be richer on the other end. Rivers thinks pairing two newcomers plus Beverley \u2014 who guarded Kevin Durant in the playoffs, while giving away seven inches \u2014 can be \u201cspecial.\u201d Utilizing three players who can legitimately guard multiple positions, the Clippers\u2019 defense could be epic, if not historic. George said: \u201cIt\u2019s going to be scary \u2026 we\u2019ve really got a chance to do something special on the defensive end. Watching Pat get out there and picking somebody up 94 feet, that\u2019s going to get me going. It\u2019s going to get Kawhi going. It\u2019s just going to become contagious on a nightly basis. I honestly think, for the first time, people are going to be excited to watch the defensive end as opposed to watching the offensive end.\u201d The makings of a unique season, then, is on deck for the Clippers. It became realistic when Leonard, fresh off a title in Toronto, chose George and the Clippers over LeBron James and Anthony Davis and the Lakers \u2014 which, in itself, seems un-Clipper-like given the club\u2019s former reputation and history, when superstars were once allergic to L.A.\u2019s \u201cother\u201d basketball team. "},{"id":31673,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/lebron-james-anthony-davis-media-day-takeaways","date":"2019-09-28","title":"Lakers ready to showcase a motivated LeBron James, hungry Anthony Davis","content":" LOS ANGELES \u2014 On training camp eve, the atmosphere, scene and vibe at the team practice complex suggested the Lakers will welcome two new and bold additions when the season tips off in three weeks. One: Anthony Davis, do-it-all forward, rescued from the depths of the New Orleans Pelicans, desperate for a championship and perhaps in line for the next Kia MVP award, both of which would be his first. Two: LeBron James. Yes, it\u2019s true this is LeBron\u2019s second season with the storied franchise, but does last year truly count? In his mind, no, it doesn\u2019t, because the Lakers and NBA were all deprived of his usual high standard of greatness and astonishing health in 2018-19. The health part betrayed him for the first time in his 16-year career, causing him to miss 27 games, mostly due to a persistently bothersome groin strain. The part about greatness didn\u2019t necessarily and totally disappear ; after all, LeBron did average 27-8-8, numbers that even stars would kill for. Except those numbers didn\u2019t translate into a playoff berth, even when he returned from injury and the Lakers still had a chance in the final month. And that, by extension, generated motivation within LeBron to answer the criticism both real (only a scant amount) and imagined (a lot) that LeBron now approaching 35 is no longer the force he was. \u201cOh, man,\u201d said teammate Kyle Kuzma. \u201cHe\u2019s going to be a load this season, more than usual.\u201d \u201cHe\u2019s gonna show all those people who are underestimating him,\u201d added Rajon Rondo. \u201cThe stuff I saw him do this summer, getting up early in the morning, first one in the gym, working hard, it\u2019s gonna pay off,\u201d Davis said. A changed LeBron? Well, it\u2019s hard to imagine him being a more focused player than before, just as it wouldn\u2019t be a stretch to suggest that, yes, LeBron could experience a slight drop-off in talent because Father Time shows no mercy to anyone. But it\u2019s also quite possible the 2019-20 LeBron can and will do what last year\u2019s version couldn\u2019t: Push the Lakers to a championship or at the very least, a deep playoff run. He appeared refreshed Friday at media day \u2014 as he should with plenty of time off. Stoic at times and totally businesslike, LeBron spoke about the frustration of watching the playoffs \u2014 he stressed he \u201cdidn\u2019t miss a single game\u201d \u2014 from his couch for the first time since 2005. He also shared his anticipation of sharing the floor with Davis. \u201cIt\u2019s exciting to have such a beautiful young mind, a beautiful player but also a great leader as well,\u201d LeBron said about Davis, although the 2018-19 Pelicans might quibble with that last part. \u201cI know the caliber of player that AD is. When Rob (Pelinka, the GM) and everyone upstairs did what they had to do to acquire a talent, person as AD, I was obviously truly excited. You saw how much time we spent together in the summer.\u201d True enough, Davis and LeBron have been shadows of one another, with Davis spending time on the set of the \u201cSpace Jam\u201d sequel, where LeBron is the star and Davis has a role, and also on the phone with Pelinka when the Lakers made decisions on the rest of the roster. The sight of Davis and LeBron, a pair of generational talents with one of them still in his prime, running the floor and causing problems for the other bench is what LeBron needed but didn\u2019t have last season when the Lakers won just 37 games and missed the playoffs for the sixth straight season. LeBron plans to be as deferential as possible to Davis, who\u2019s coming off a bitter end to a six-year run in New Orleans, in order to get the best from his All-Star forward. If that means LeBron must allow Davis to be the focal point of the offense, LeBron says so be it. \u201cIf we\u2019re not playing through Anthony Davis while he\u2019s on the floor, then it makes no sense to have him on the floor,\u201d James said. \u201cBecause he\u2019s that great.\u201d The goal, obviously, is for LeBron to develop the same chemistry with Davis that he had with Dwyane Wade in Miami, and to get similar results \u2014 the Heat won a pair of championships and reached the NBA Finals every year with LeBron in the fold. The process is a bit more critical now because the Lakers sacrificed a chunk of their future to get Davis, and LeBron has only three years left on his contract. There\u2019s also the notion that LeBron is in his sunset years although the insinuation, according to LeBron, is that it means he\u2019s lost a step and a place among the league\u2019s great players. While some of this criticism might be generated by his imagination, there was talk this summer \u2014 such as comments from David Griffin \u2014 that might have bothered him a little bit. \u201cI\u2019m very motivated,\u201d he said, \u201cbut right now I\u2019m in \u2018not talking about it mode.\u2019 I\u2019ve been very quiet this summer for a reason \u2026 but there\u2019s some motivation for me. There\u2019s a lot of conversations going on this summer and I\u2019m just very quiet, very quiet. And I\u2019m just going to maintain quiet, My mother always taught me, \u2018don\u2019t talk about it, be about it.\u2019 So that\u2019s where I\u2019m at. I think as a team, and myself, we need to get the Lakers back to what they\u2019ve been accustomed to over the years. I\u2019m excited about that.\u201d LeBron needs Davis and yet, Davis needs LeBron just as much \u2014 the projected 2019-20 LeBron, who\u2019s juiced by motivation, failure, an injury setback and all that chatter that he hears (or doesn\u2019t) about his declining skills. Because without LeBron, Davis wouldn\u2019t be here. Davis would either still be in New Orleans or staring up at the banners hanging from the ceiling in Boston and wondering how to duplicate that. Therefore, until further notice, the fate of the Lakers will rest with how much LeBron can distance himself from last season. The Lakers will require improved outside shooting and better defense (especially from LeBron) and obviously an MVP-level season from Davis to place themselves in the championship conversation . Then, all of the above are realistic. Under the new experimental NBA G League rule, one free throw worth one, two or three points will be awarded in the event of any foul that would typically result in one, two or three free throws being shot under standard NBA rules. The experimental free throw rule will not apply during the last two minutes of the fourth quarter or the entirety of any overtime period. The NBA G League will continue to play with experimental rules that were previously implemented, including the transition take foul, the 14-second shot clock reset on an advance, a two-minute overtime period, the away-from-the-play foul rule and the reset timeout. The reset allows teams to call a timeout to advance the ball and make substitutions but not huddle in the final two minutes of the fourth quarter and during entire overtime periods. Apart from experimental rules, NBA G League games are played under all other NBA rules. The research and development arm of the NBA, the NBA G League routinely tests experimental rules and procedures. This season, the NBA implemented the Coach\u2019s Challenge, which was first tested in the NBA G League in the 2014-15 season. An increase in fines for tampering, for entering into unauthorized agreements with players and even for talking about players under contract elsewhere passed unanimously, commissioner Adam Silver said, in a vote of the Board of Governors. Final figures still were to be determined, though reports have suggested the maximum fines could rise to $10 million for tampering, $6 million for improper deals and $5 million for comments enticing other teams\u2019 players.  Tougher penalties, however, only matter if the league\u2019s 30 franchises have the will to do what it takes to impose them. And the discipline not to do what triggers them. The meetings this week and Friday\u2019s vote didn\u2019t only give Silver a bigger stick to wield against such violations, they encouraged him to use it. The message of the Board? \u201cY ou need to do a better job enforcing the rules that are already on your books,\u201d Silver said, \u201cand do a better job ensuring that there is a culture around the league where people believe there are absolute consequences if you don\u2019t play by the rules.\u201d The frenzied free agent market this offseason, for instance, raised red flags about teams\u2019 compliance with rules dictating when front-office executives and players\u2019 representatives could begin negotiations. The number and enormity of deals that leaked out within minutes of the June 30 tipoff suggested that contract talks in many cases surely began before the designated period. Also, as free agent Kawhi Leonard pondered his decision to leave Toronto (eventually signing with the Clippers), there was speculation that his representative may have sought benefits outside the salary-cap provisions. Tampering is a transgression that\u2019s more troubling to some teams than others. While clubs such as Charlotte, Indiana and anyone who has a player Houston covets want rules to be strictly enforced, the Los Angeles Lakers \u2013 dinged in the recent past for talking publicly about Paul George and Giannis Antetokounmpo while they still were under contract \u2013 have fared well in flouting them. The Boston Celtics, meanwhile, might have found themselves on both side of the issue in losing guard Kyrie Irving to Brooklyn and forward Al Horford to Philadelphia, while luring guard Kemba Walker away from the Hornets. But the position of the league Friday was that all the organizations favor more integrity and less chicanery, whether to avoid being victimized or to not get outmaneuvered by some rival. \u201cThere was a strong view of every single person in the room that we need to ensure that we\u2019re creating a culture of compliance in this league,\u201d Silver said. \u201cOur teams want to know that they\u2019re competing on a level playing field, and frankly don\u2019t want to feel disadvantaged if they are adhering to our existing rules.\u201d \u201cCulture of compliance\u201d was mentioned repeatedly by Silver, who presides over a league that, like most others, needs teams to strike a balance between staying competitive and being cooperative. If zealous owners, presidents of basketball operations or general managers go too far in one direction, there\u2019s chaos. If they go too far in the other, they risk getting criticized and even slapped with a collusion lawsuit for not pursuing or bidding for players.  \u201cWe don\u2019t have that problem,\u201d one member of the Board said at the conclusion of Friday\u2019s session. Integrity and transparency have become buzzwords around the halls of Olympic Tower, the NBA\u2019s headquarters in New York, as they relate to traditional priorities such as fans\u2019 trust and new ones such as legal sports betting. For instance, the decision this week to have coaches submit their starting lineups earlier \u2013 from 10 minutes prior to tipoff to 30 minutes beginning this season \u2013 is widely seen as a nod to wagering, providing more time to know which key players will or won\u2019t be available for a given game. (Teams will be permitted to amend those lineups if a player sustains or aggravates an injury during pregame warmups.) Dialing up the dollar amounts was the big move Friday, but Silver has other \u201ctools\u201d in his box to penalize teams that might view fines as a cost of doing business if it helps them land a prized free agent. Remember, the Clippers were fined $50,000 in May after coach Doc Rivers compared Leonard to Michael Jordan in an ESPN interview; two months later, Leonard was on Rivers\u2019 roster. The league already had the authority to strip draft picks, suspend team personnel and void contracts for the most egregious violations. \u201cF ining authority unto itself may be one of the least effective tools,\u201d Silver said. \u201cAll of those [other] provisions are on the table.\u201d Enforcing the rules, beyond just imposing penalties after the fact, will require some serious policing by the NBA. Owners and top basketball executives will be required to certify that they will not engage in improper negotiations with players or their reps, giving the league more clout if they subsequently violate the rules. Five teams reportedly will be audited annually, with a framework on the extent of the league\u2019s reach still in the works.  Silver confirmed that he has the power to take people\u2019s cell phones, tablets and other devices, if necessary. While he\u2019s sensitive to privacy concerns, the commissioner added: \u201cIt\u2019s my job to create an appropriate amount of tension in that area. Obviously, if people felt that they were absolutely free and clear to communicate in certain ways, you wouldn\u2019t be addressing the consequences notion of improper activity.\u201d One area not addressed by the Board of Governors was the role of players in recruiting other teams\u2019 stars, not just in advance of any official free-agent negotiating period but while their friends still have years remaining on their contracts. Last season, New Orleans big man Anthony Davis undermined the Pelicans\u2019 and his individual season when \u2013 at what many believe to be the suggestion of agent Rich Paul\u2019s and \/ or fellow Paul client LeBron James \u2013 he asked to be traded to the Lakers halfway through his five-year extension with his team. The league fined Davis $50,000 for that disruption but, sure enough, Davis and the $55.8 million left on his contract were dealt to Los Angeles in July. Silver reminded his audience that some issues must be collectively bargained with the National Basketball Players Association. For example, moving the start of free agency up to begin before the Draft would be one of those. The league historically has not enforced tampering rules against player-to-player contact. None of the measures mentioned Friday addressed that. \u201cWhat\u2019s lost sometimes,\u201d Silver said, \u201cis that for the 450 players or so in the league, they want a competitive landscape as well. They don\u2019t necessarily want a system where there\u2019s a sense that certain teams have a competitive advantage over other teams, because then you\u2019re just benefiting the players that happen to be on those teams.\u201d Even as reports of tougher penalties and more thorough rules were being published this week, some team executives were speculating to media folks about ways they could be bent or circumvented. But Silver did not sound deterred. \u201cMy sense of the room was this was not just about \u2018league office vs. teams,\u2019 that what we are really seeking again is a cultural change,\u201d the commissioner said. \u201cIf someone is absolutely determined to cheat in any industry and people are willing to do anything to be successful, I guess you have rogue actors in every field and in every industry. \u201cWhat we\u2019re saying, though, [is] we think we\u2019re dramatically going to increase the likelihood that we\u2019re going to catch you. I don\u2019t want to suggest there\u2019s any perfect system. At some point you\u2019re relying, at least in part, on the good faith of partners working together and \u2026 that this is a culture in which people want to compete fairly.\u201d That\u2019s the challenge, at least. Fines of up to $10 million are now possible in the most egregious situations, along with forfeiture of draft picks, suspensions of executives and voiding of contracts when rule breaking is found \u2014 significant enough threats, the league hopes, to end any notion of teams entering into deals with free agents before rules allow. \u201cWe need to ensure that we\u2019re creating a culture of compliance in this league,\u201d NBA Commissioner Adam Silver said after two days of meetings concluded in New York. \u201cOur teams want to know that they\u2019re competing on a level playing field and frankly don\u2019t want to feel disadvantaged if they are adhering to our existing rules.\u201d The rules aren\u2019t new, but Silver has been saying for months that it\u2019s pointless for the league to have policies that cannot be enforced. And while the new parameters aren\u2019t foolproof, an important change is that every franchise will have to annually certify that its executives did not to free agents or their representatives before league rules allow. But for years, the notion of waiting for the start of free agency to talk to available players has been largely ignored. This year, free agency was to officially begin at 6 p.m. Eastern on June 30, and many deals were known to be done within minutes. \u201cThere need to be consequences when rules are violated,\u201d Silver said. The league told teams last week that fines would be raised in part to reflect the 600% increase in league revenue and the 1,100% increase in franchise value since the maximum-fine ceilings were last touched in 1996. There are some elements of the new measures that still need to be worked out \u2014 specifically, the specifics behind the league\u2019s new mandate that five teams will be randomly selected for investigatory audits to see if there were any rule-compliance issues. The NBA wants teams to keep records of talks with players and agents for a year, and the league has the power to review a team\u2019s electronic communications devices. The NBA is revising rule-book language regarding traveling, and specifically defining a \u201cgather\u201d \u2014 plus clarifying how many steps a player may take. For players receiving a pass or picking up a loose ball, the gather is defined as when control of the ball is gained. Off the dribble, the definition is when a player has two hands on the ball, or brings it to a pause, or otherwise gains control. The league is expected to release a training video next week, and said correctly calling travels gather will be a point of emphasis this season. Daily fantasy players and bettors will now know who is expected to play in a certain game a bit earlier than usual. Teams now must submit starting lineups 30 minutes before the scheduled start time, instead of the previous rule of 10 minutes. Lineups can still change after the 30-minute mark, which gives teams flexibility if an injury occurs or is aggravated during warm-ups. The revision will not change the substance of the rule but will help eliminate the gap between the rule as written and how it has been applied in NBA games. \u201cOne of the most misunderstood rules in our game is how traveling is interpreted and appropriately called,\u201d said Byron Spruell, NBA President, League Operations. \u201cRevising the language of certain areas of the rule is part of our three-pronged approach to address the uncertainty around traveling. This approach also includes an enforcement plan to make traveling a point of emphasis for our officiating staff, along with an aggressive education plan to increase understanding of the rule by players, coaches, media and fans.\u201d The official NBA rule book will now have a section that formally defines the \u201cgather,\u201d which is a concept that has been used by the officiating staff for many years to apply the rule but was never defined in the rule book. The text of the rule will also be revised to provide additional clarity regarding how many steps a player may take after the gather occurs. This type of change is most likely to occur if a player sustains or reaggravates an injury during pregame warm-ups. Drafted 10th overall in the 2001 NBA Draft by the Boston Celtics, Johnson averaged 20-plus points in five straight seasons (2005-10) as a member of the Atlanta Hawks. It\u2019s now nine-years-and-counting in the top spot for the U.S., which has held the No. 1 ranking since winning the 2010 world championship. World Cup champion Spain stayed No. 2, Australia leaped eight spots to No. 3, World Cup finalist Argentina rose one spot to No. 4 and World Cup bronze-medalist France fell two slots to No. 5. FIBA\u2019s rankings take results from the most recent eight years into account \u2014 which means the U.S. is still reaping point benefits from the 2012 and 2016 Olympic gold medals and the 2014 World Cup title. \u201cIn this day and age, basketball in other countries is not a secret,\u201d U.S. coach Gregg Popovich said after the Americans completed their run in the World Cup. \u201cSo it\u2019s not like there\u2019s an epiphany or a revelation to be made. There are wonderful teams and wonderful coaches all over the world. You go compete and the best teams win.\u201d It\u2019s now expected that the U.S. will retain the No. 1 ranking going into the 2020 Tokyo Olympics. Several top NBA players, including Stephen Curry, Draymond Green and Damian Lillard have said in recent days that they intend to play for the U.S. in Tokyo, where the Americans will try to win a fourth consecutive gold medal. Most top U.S. players declined to be part of the World Cup team. \u201cI\u2019m expecting them to be so strong next year,\u201d Spain coach Sergio Scariolo said. The new rankings confirmed that European champion Slovenia, which didn\u2019t earn a spot in the World Cup field after many of its top players couldn\u2019t take part in qualifying since those games conflicted with the NBA and Euroleague schedules, will still have a chance to compete in the Olympics \u2014 as will seven other teams that found out they\u2019re headed to playoffs next year. Angola, Senegal, Mexico, Uruguay, China, Korea and Croatia also still have Olympic hopes. Those last eight playoff spots awarded Thursday went to the top two teams from Africa, Europe, Asia-Oceania and the Americas regions who hadn\u2019t either already clinched Olympic berths or spots in the last-chance playoffs. Japan is automatically qualified for the 12-team Olympic tournament as the host country. The U.S., Argentina, Nigeria, Spain, France, Iran and Australia clinched Olympic spots at the World Cup by finishing as the best teams in their respective FIBA regions \u2014 the Americas, Africa, Europe, Asia and Oceania. That leaves four unclaimed Olympic berths, and 24 teams to compete for them in playoffs next year. There will be four six-team tournaments held from June 23-28, 2020 \u2014 winner-take-all, all in this case meaning an Olympic berth. Bidding for sites is expected to begin shortly, FIBA said. The other 16 playoff spots were awarded based on World Cup placing. They went to Serbia, Lithuania, Greece, Russia, Brazil, Italy, Puerto Rico, Turkey, the Dominican Republic, Venezuela, Germany, Canada, the Czech Republic, Poland, New Zealand and Tunisia. Belize was the top mover in the new rankings, climbing 50 spots to No. 118. Kosovo rose 21 spots to No. 69, Togo went up 21 spots to No. 136, Tunisia climbed 18 spots to No. 33 and Ivory Coast went up 16 spots to No. 48. FIBA has four sets of rankings \u2014 for men, women, boys and girls. The U.S. holds the No. 1 spot in all four of those rankings, though the race is tightest among the men. The U.S. men hold a lead of 54.9 points over Spain in those rankings, while the rankings margins held by the U.S. women (310 points over No. 2 Spain), boys (291 points over No. 2 Canada) and girls (155 points over No. 2 Spain) are far more comfortable."},{"id":31764,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/wnba-elena-delle-donne-mvp-2019-official-release","date":"2019-09-19","title":"Elena Delle Donne named 2019 WNBA Most Valuable Player","content":" NEW YORK \u2013 Washington Mystics forward-guard Elena Delle Donne has been named the 2019 WNBA Most Valuable Player, the WNBA announced today. The seven-year veteran has won her second MVP award and become the first player in WNBA history to earn the honor with two different teams. She was also selected as MVP in 2015 as a member of the Chicago Sky. As the Mystics\u2019 first MVP winner, Delle Donne joins five other WNBA players who have multiple MVP trophies. Lauren Jackson, Lisa Leslie and Sheryl Swoopes have all been named MVP three times, while Cynthia Cooper and Candace Parker have won the award twice each. Delle Donne received 41 of 43 first-place votes and a total of 420 points from a national panel of sportswriters and broadcasters. Phoenix Mercury center Brittney Griner finished second with 167 points. Connecticut Sun forward-center Jonquel Jones (145 points) was third, followed by Los Angeles Sparks forward Nneka Ogwumike (128) and Seattle Storm forward Natasha Howard (121). Sky guard Courtney Vandersloot received the other two first-place votes and finished sixth with 81 points. Players were awarded 10 points for a first-place vote, seven points for a second-place vote, five points for a third-place vote, three points for a fourth-place vote and one point for a fifth-place vote. The 6-5 Delle Donne, who led Washington to a league-best 26-8 record and the No. 1 seed in the 2019 WNBA Playoffs, will be presented with the MVP award tonight before the Mystics host the Las Vegas Aces. Game 2 of the WNBA Semifinals series will tip off at 8:30 p.m. ET on ESPN2. Washington leads the best-of-five series 1-0. Delle Donne ranked second in the WNBA in scoring (19.5 ppg), fifth in rebounding (8.3 rpg) and 11th in blocked shots (1.29 bpg) while playing 31 games this season. She became the first player in WNBA history to shoot at least 50 percent from the field (51.5), 40 percent from three-point range (43.0) and 90 percent from the free throw line (WNBA-high 97.4). The Wilmington, Del., native posted the highest free throw percentage ever for a player with at least 100 attempts (114-of-117) and made her last 64 attempts of the regular season. She also ranked seventh in the league in field goal percentage and fourth in three-point field goal percentage. With Delle Donne leading the way, the Mystics recorded the highest single-season offensive rating in WNBA history, scoring 112.9 points per 100 possessions. Delle Donne\u2019s superlatives in 2019 included being voted to the WNBA All-Star Game for the sixth time and sweeping all three Eastern Conference Player of the Month honors. She was also named the WNBA Eastern Conference Player of the Week seven times, matching Tina Charles\u2019 record for the most Player of the Week honors in a conference in a season. Delle Donne, 30, was selected by the Sky with the No. 2 overall pick in the 2013 WNBA Draft. She spent four seasons with Chicago before joining the Mystics prior to the 2017 season. At the University of Delaware, she was a two-time consensus All-America First Team selection and three-time Colonial Athletic Conference Player of the Year. The Warriors have played full seasons in each of The Bay\u2019s three major cities: Oakland, San Francisco and San Jose. * The Town \u2013 City Edition: A tribute to Oakland first introduced during the 2017-18 season, The Town uniform features the logo for the city of Oakland in white set on a black jersey. The uniform celebrates the Oakland community and its support for the Warriors, who played 47 of the previous 48 seasons in The Town. * San Francisco \u2013 Classic Edition: A throwback to the Warriors\u2019 original Bay Area jersey worn upon the team\u2019s arrival to San Francisco from Philadelphia in 1962, the San Francisco Classic Edition jersey features the city\u2019s namesake across the chest of the white jersey in a color palate of navy, gold and red. A yellow version of the uniform was worn by the Warriors as a throwback during the 2009-10 season. * The City \u2013 Classic Edition: Designed by the team\u2019s larger-than-life owner Franklin Mieuli in 1966-67, The City Classic Edition includes a pair of iconic San Francisco symbols, featuring the Golden Gate Bridge on the front and a cable car on the back of the yellow jersey. The Warriors have worn the throwback several times since the team\u2019s last season in San Francisco in 1970-71, most recently donning the yellow jersey during the 2015-16 campaign. "},{"id":31800,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/jerry-colangelo-usa-showing-fiba-world-cup","date":"2019-09-17","title":"Jerry Colangelo laments Team USA's showing at FIBA World Cup","content":" A seventh-place showing at the FIBA World Cup made the 2019 edition of the U.S. Men\u2019s National Team the first American team of NBA players to lose since the 2006 World Championship. That finish wasn\u2019t lost on USA Basketball managing director Jerry Colangelo, who has overseen the program since taking it over on April 27, 2005. In an interview with SI.com\u2019s Chris Mannix, Colangelo sounded determined to get Team USA back on track on the international stage. \u201cThere has not been any disappointment around USA Basketball in a while,\u201d Colangelo told SI.com . \u201cThis will bother me until the 2020 Olympics.\u201d Next summer, Colangelo will end his 14-year tenure atop USA Basketball and has seen it win gold in the 2008, \u201912 and \u201916 Olympics. Additionally, Team USA won the FIBA World Cup title in 2010 (the U.S. team\u2019s first there since 1994) and in \u201914. Despite the disappointing finish this year, Colangelo wasn\u2019t about to draw parallels between this team and the 2002 World Cup squad that is seen as one of the low points in Team USA history. \u201cYou can\u2019t compare the two years,\u201d Colangelo told SI.com. \u201cIt\u2019s apples and oranges.\u201d He did take some issue with the NBA superstars who opted to not play in the FIBA World Cup this year. Among the NBA standouts who opted out of playing were Anthony Davis, James Harden, Damian Lillard, CJ McCollum, Bradley Beal, DeMar DeRozan and others. \u201cThe disappointment I feel is not from the guys who said they wouldn\u2019t play,\u201d Colangelo told SI.com. \u201cIt\u2019s those that said they would, and then backed out.\u201d Davis, Lillard and Harden were late withdrawals from Team USA, but that may not hurt them in being a part of the U.S. National Team come the 2020 Olympics. \u201cWe\u2019ll deal with those cases individually,\u201d Colangelo said. \u201cIt\u2019s important to field as strong a team as possible.\u201d In each of the last five major international tournaments, the U.S. ranked No. 1 in offensive efficiency. Through its first six games of the 2019 FIBA World Cup, it ranked ninth offensively. Before breaking with a 12-for-25 performance against Poland on Saturday in the seventh-place game, the Americans had shot just 33.3 percent from 3-point range, well below the NBA league average (35.5 percent), even though the 3-point distance is shorter on the FIBA floor. Though the U.S. was one of the best defensive teams in the 2019 FIBA World Cup, it couldn\u2019t turn enough stops into transition opportunities. In each of the five major tournaments that the U.S. won from 2008 to 2016, it ranked first or second in pace. Through its first six games, this U.S. team ranked 13th of 32 World Cup teams in pace (an estimated 75 possessions per 40 minutes). After the win against Poland to close out FIBA play, coach Gregg Popovich defended his team while also sounding off on the notion Team USA is always a shoo-in for gold. \u201cIf you don\u2019t win, some people will play the blame game,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cThere\u2019s no blame to be placed anywhere. Companies that make clothing and shoes for the National Basketball Association players are in the crosshairs of President Donald Trump\u2019s escalating China trade wars. So, the question is, will American fans of sports stars like Los Angeles Lakers\u2019 James be willing to pay higher prices for the gear? The stakes are high as U.S. sales from sports licensed merchandise including NBA items rang up $21 billion last year, according to Licensing International, a trade group. Sales on NBAStore.com rose 15% during the 12-month period through August, according to the league. And many of the sports brands ranging from Adidas to Puma rely on China for at least some of their sourcing. Moreover, experts worry China could impose penalties on Western brands who sell there at a time when business in that country is exploding. Some also believe U.S. fans might turn to counterfeit merchandise if they don\u2019t want to pay higher prices. * LeBron, Lakers top NBA merchandise list in 2018-19   \u201cWhen you raise prices on legitimate goods, you encourage the production of illegitimate goods,\u201d said Steve Lamar, executive vice president of The American Apparel and Footwear Association, a trade group. \u201cWe\u2019re definitely seeing pressure on brands. We\u2019re just waiting for the other basketball shoe to drop.\u201d Until now, consumers were largely spared from higher prices in Trump\u2019s previous round of import taxes. That has changed. Starting Sept. 1, the U .S. government began collecting 15 percent on $112 billion in Chinese imports, on a wide array of merchandise including basketball jerseys, basketball shoes, basketballs and even hoops. Higher tariffs are set to hit another batch of Chinese products \u2014 $160 billion worth on Dec. 15 and include other sports products, according to the American Apparel & Footwear Association. President Trump tweeted Wednesday that planned tariff increases on another $250 billion in Chinese imports, which would include sports bags, would be delayed until Oct. 15, from Oct. 1. Tariff increases are set to go from 25% to 30%. Many sporting goods companies, including Adidas, Under Armour and Spaulding declined to comment on how their business is being affected by the China trade wars. But like many companies, sport brands have been diversifying their sourcing away from China to factories in Vietnam and Bangladesh for the last several years even before escalating tensions between the U.S. and China. Under Armour has been working for several years to reduce sourcing in China. \u201cWith current tariffs, we actually are not being affected very much at all, \u201d Patrick Fisk, president and chief operating officer at Under Armour told CNBC last week. \u201cWe only have 10 percent of what comes into the U.S. from China. So the current state, we\u2019re OK.\u201d Puma announced earlier this year a new multi-year partnership that will make the international sports brand an official marketing partner of the NBA. \u201cOur sector in China has been very strong. We\u2019ve been growing 15% every quarter,\u201d says Puma U.S. CEO Bjoern Gulden, noting it\u2019s the fastest growing market ahead of the U.S. and Europe. But he added, \u201cTariffs and trade wars are not good for the market. It carries uncertainty.\u201d Puma has been moving its sourcing out of China over the past two years and now the country accounts for 20 percent of its overall production. Still, Gulden says costs are going up, and he\u2019s not sure whether the company will have to raise prices. Gulden and others believe that the top end of the market may be less vulnerable than the lower end. For customers who buy sneakers ranging from $150 to $250, an increase may not hurt sales, but that could be a different story for customers who buy shoes in the $60 to $70 range, he said. Still, he says no one \u201chas an appetite for higher prices.\u201d The tensions between the U.S. and China come as many sports brands have been digging deeper into China where basketball is a massive business and the NBA\u2019s fan base is exploding through social media. The good news is that American brands including Nike who sell there say business remains strong and they haven\u2019t seen consumers in China pull back because of the strain. \u201cWe have not seen any impact on our business to-date and we continue to see strong momentum as we enter fiscal year 2020, \u201d Mark G. Parker, chairman, CEO and president of Nike told analysts during a conference call following its fiscal fourth quarter earnings in June. It reported revenue growth in China up 21% this past fiscal year. Nike says it produces about a quarter of its product in China for the globe. However, its exposure in terms of product produced in China to North America is \u201crelatively modest.\u201d There\u2019s a silver lining for sportswear makers to Trump\u2019s trade war with China, however. Puma\u2019s Gulden says that the company is using the same factories in China that used to produce merchandise for the American market for the Chinese market. Previously, factories outside of China produced goods for China. Now, Puma can stay on top of trends faster. \u201cYou are much quicker. No duty. The local coaches working with him didn\u2019t know a lot about the game. Barely anyone noticed that an NBA player was in town. Basketball wasn\u2019t a big deal in China. And then everything changed very quickly. The footprint of the NBA has grown at an extremely rapid pace over the last two decades in China, where more than 500 million people watched games last season and where one new streaming deal alone will pump $1.5 billion into the league\u2019s coffers over the next five years. \u201cWhen I first came here, I never thought the game in China would get to be this big,\u201d Bryant said. \u201cBut it has. And it\u2019s not going to stop.\u201d The possibilities seem endless. Could there be an NBA team in China despite the travel that would be involved? Might there be two-way player contracts between the NBA and the Chinese Basketball Association? What about the NBA constructing a team to play in China or the Chinese sending a team for a full season in the U.S.? Farfetched as all that may sound, keep in mind that 20 years ago no one envisioned the NBA-China relationship to be this big \u2014 or that it would keep growing after Yao Ming\u2019s run with the Houston Rockets ended eight years ago. The NBA has academies in China now, and the Chinese national team returned to the NBA Summer League in Las Vegas this year. \u201cIt\u2019s a good question,\u201d Golden State coach Steve Kerr said. \u201cI think the next step will probably come when the next Yao Ming comes. That would take it to a new level, more Chinese players to reach the NBA and make an impact.\u201d The marriage between the NBA and the world\u2019s most populous country is stronger than ever. NBA officials say more than 300 million Chinese people play the game and 40 million are registered to play the 2K video game. Thousands showed up this summer just to watch the sons of Dwyane Wade and LeBron James play exhibitions with the rest of their high school teammates. A trade war is happening between the U.S. and China, political tensions are escalating between the countries and it could impact the products of the league\u2019s business partners. But the game itself continues to thrive. \u201cI think sports transcends politics and I hope the NBA can continue to connect fans globally,\u201d Dallas Mavericks owner Mark Cuban said. \u201cI don\u2019t have any reason to think our relationship won\u2019t continue to be positive.\u201d Nothing seems to be able to derail the NBA\u2019s popularity. The team that the U.S. sent to the World Cup in China didn\u2019t feature the NBA\u2019s biggest stars, yet drew sellout crowds for each of its first six games. U.S. coach Gregg Popovich was begged for autographs and selfies everywhere he went. \u201cWe\u2019ve known for a long time how big basketball has become in China, of course, but all over the world,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cIt\u2019s an international deal now. There are so many great players in so many countries. It\u2019s not a secret.\u201d Stars like James, Stephen Curry, and James Harden have a trip to China on their annual schedules \u2014 and when Wade, the recently retired guard who has a lifetime contract with Chinese shoe company Li-Ning, visited this summer one of his events had to be halted after about 10 minutes because the mall where it was happening was overflowing with people. Donovan Mitchell of the Utah Jazz has been to China twice this summer, once to promote his brand, the second time for the World Cup with USA Basketball. He sees it becoming an annual stop for him, too \u2014 and believes there is no ceiling for the game globally. \u201cMan, I couldn\u2019t tell you,\u201d Mitchell said. \u201cI think it\u2019s going to be even bigger and it\u2019s not going to be just China. It\u2019s going to be many more countries. The (relationship) between the NBA and China has been huge since I was a kid and it can only take off from there \u2026 because the passion and love is so strong.\u201d It\u2019s not a one-sided relationship; China sees reason to invest in the NBA. Joe Tsai, the co-founder of Chinese e-commerce giant Alibaba, agreed this summer to buy the remaining 51% that he didn\u2019t already own of the Brooklyn Nets and Barclays Center from Mikhail Prokhorov in deals worth about $3.4 billion. In 2016, Lizhang Jiang, a businessman from Shanghai, bought 5% of the Minnesota Timberwolves, a stake he sold earlier this year. China also takes immense pride in players like Klay Thompson wearing Chinese brands on the court. (Thompson has a 10-year deal with Chinese shoe company Anta for a reported $80 million.) And China sent its national team to NBA Summer League this past July primarily to get ready for the World Cup, but also for exposure on the NBA stage. \u201cI think it\u2019s good for our players and good for the team,\u201d China coach Li Nan said of playing in Las Vegas. \u201cI think it\u2019s good for everyone.\u201d The NBA has opened three basketball academies in China and has seen very quick success with academies in Asia and Africa. The international influence on the league was more present this past season than ever. The NBA MVP, Giannis Antetokounmpo, is from Greece. The rookie of the year, Luka Doncic, is from Slovenia. The most improved player, Pascal Siakam, is from Cameroon. The defensive player of the year, Rudy Gobert, is from France. The All-NBA center, Nikola Jokic, is from Serbia. \u201cThis past summer, an NBA Academy prospect from China signed a contract with a National Basketball League team in Australia, becoming the first male NBA Academy prospect from China to sign a contract with a professional team,\u201d NBA Commissioner Adam Silver said. \u201cAnd on the women\u2019s side, Han Xu from the New York Liberty, who trained at the NBA Academy in Shandong, China, became the first NBA Academy prospect to be drafted into the NBA or WNBA.\u201d It hasn\u2019t happened overnight. Former Commissioner David Stern struck a deal with Chinese television to show games on tape-delay three decades ago, and once toyed with the idea of some sort of NBA-sponsored or branded league in China. Teams embrace the chance to play the annual preseason games in China because he exposure is worth the jet lag. \u201cWhen I have 76ers gear on and I walk through Shanghai, walk through Shenzhen, if I had a nickel for every time somebody said \u2018Trust the process\u2019 in perfect English I wouldn\u2019t be standing here working,\u201d Philadelphia 76ers CEO Scott O\u2019Neil said, referencing the team\u2019s motto during its rebuilding phase of recent years. \u201cWe\u2019re very much a part of the fabric of China.\u201d None of this seemed possible 20 years ago or so, when Bryant made that first trip. Now fans can\u2019t get enough. \u201cWhen you come here, you feel it from the fans, their energy, people at the hotel, people just walking around,\u201d Kerr said in China during the World Cup. \u201cEverybody just seems very excited about basketball.\u201d Same goes for the game\u2019s future in China."},{"id":31767,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/report-nets-hiring-david-levy-ceo","date":"2019-09-16","title":"Report: Nets hiring former Turner president David Levy as CEO","content":" The Brooklyn Nets are continuing their offseason makeover with another change in the front office by reportedly hiring David Levy.
