Schedule"},{"id":32087,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/team-usa-notebook-fiba-world-cup-prep","date":"2019-08-30","title":"Team USA Notebook: Sense of purpose permeates as tipoff nears","content":" SHANGHAI \u2014 The U.S. Men\u2019s National Team held their second practice in Shanghai on Friday, with one more day before they open the World Cup with a game against the Czech Republic on Sunday ( 8:30 a.m. ET ). It turned out to be their final pre-competition practice, because head coach Gregg Popovich canceled their session for Saturday. Once the competition starts, the U.S. will be playing every other day, with three changes of location between the first round and the semifinals (should the Americans make it there). So practice time could be somewhat limited going forward. But the games, against new and unfamiliar opponents, are arguably better opportunities to get better than practices. The first few games should come without much pressure, and maybe it\u2019s a good thing that the Americans have already been through a pressure situation in their preparation for the World Cup. Of course, the U.S. lost that second exhibition game to Australia last Saturday. The Americans had issues on both ends of the floor, but really, it was their defense that really let them down, allowing 98 points on 84 Australia possessions (1.17 per). It was an exhibition, but it was the first loss by an all-NBA-player U.S. team since the semifinals of the 2006 World Championship. That\u2019s a long winning streak to see come to an end. \u201cObviously, it sucked in the moment,\u201d Brook Lopez said about the loss. \u201cBut it was definitely good for us, looking ahead to the World Cup.\u201d Defense is about effort and energy. And in a 40-minute game, consistent effort and energy is all the more important. \u201cWe can\u2019t take part of a game for granted and can\u2019t have our level of intensity ever drop,\u201d Lopez said. \u201cIf anything, it has to increase throughout each and every game. We relented as a group. After we beat Australia in the first game, they came out with everything they had. It showed us a little glimpse of the focus and concentration we have to have the entire time here in China.\u201d The following-day film session wasn\u2019t easy, but according to Kemba Walker, they didn\u2019t need it to figure out what went wrong. \u201cI think we knew before we even watched film,\u201d Walker said. \u201cIt was tough, and you know, Pop can be pretty tough. We knew, and I think that\u2019s why we came out against Canada [on Monday] the way we did. It was a very humbling loss. And hopefully that [feeling] is going to get us over that hump.\u201d The win over Canada was the U.S. Team\u2019s worst offensive performance of its exhibition slate, but the overmatched Canadians scored just once on their first 10 possessions of the game (and just nine points in the first quarter). The U.S. can smother some of these lesser talented teams (like the ones they\u2019ll face in Group E). But against the best teams in the tournament (like Australia, who they could face in the quarterfinals), there has to be both effort and cohesion defensively. \u201cThey\u2019ve got a very unselfish team that passes the ball very well,\u201d Lopez said. \u201c[Andrew] Bogut, especially, is such a huge hub for them.\u201d Bogut suffered an ankle injury in Australia\u2019s exhibition loss to Germany on Wednesday, but is reportedly \u201cprobable\u201d for their opener against Canada on Sunday .  Myles Turner was one of the United States\u2019 best players over their five-game exhibition slate. Not only did he put up boxscore numbers (averaging 15.2 points and 12.7 rebounds), but the U.S. was also at its best with him on the floor , outscoring its opponents by 48 points in his 83 minutes. That Turner emerged as the go-to center was somewhat of a relief to USA Basketball managing director Jerry Colangelo, who wasn\u2019t sure what he was going to get out of his group of big men. \u201cWe were looking for someone to come out of the pack of the bigs, and he has,\u201d Colangelo said Friday. \u201cHe\u2019s had a couple of major rebounding games. He\u2019s very active. If he keeps active, he\u2019s going to get rebounds and he\u2019s going to block some shots.\u201d Colangelo wasn\u2019t totally surprised by Turner\u2019s play, though. \u201cI had expectations that he could be [the starting center],\u201d he said, \u201cbecause I was told that he\u2019s had a great summer in terms of his personal work.\u201d Good news for the U.S., and maybe good news for the Indiana Pacers. Popovich was asked what he wants to do in his free time in China. Alas, free time is limited when you have games every other day. \u201cThere are things that I would like to do,\u201d Popovich said, \u201cthat I know that I will not have time to do, because the focus is on what we\u2019re doing here.\u201d What is it that he\u2019d really like to do? Well, the coach is an explorer. \u201cMostly to get out and walk,\u201d he said, \u201cto see neighborhoods and walk and be with nobody, not be able to speak the language, and feel like an idiot. \u201cJust walk around, walk into a place, see what happens and see what you see. It\u2019s more fun when you\u2019re in another country and you just take off. You don\u2019t assume anything and you don\u2019t have people tell you where to go. You just see where you end up. I don\u2019t know if I\u2019m going to have the chance to do that, so I\u2019m going to go to restaurants at night.\u201d The U.S. plays its first game on Sunday, but the World Cup gets started on Saturday with games in Groups A, B, C and D . A couple of Saturday games \u2013 Poland vs. Venezuela in Group A and Nigeria vs. Russia in Group B \u2013 are between what look to be the second and third best teams in those groups. And because two teams from each group advance to the second round, those first-day matchups could end up determining which teams make it through. That means we\u2019ll get our first NBA action next month with the preseason slate beginning on the 30th. Training camps will be opening, media days will take place and before we know it, we\u2019ll be tipping off the 2019-20 season on Oct. 22. It feels like opening night is within arm\u2019s reach, right? Not quite. It\u2019s still August. And so, as the doldrums of the NBA offseason continue, we\u2019re looking back at the 10 best scorers in the fourth quarter \u2014 a moment not every player is built for \u2014 during the 2018-19 season. To be clear, this isn\u2019t an opinion piece. It\u2019s a factual list \u2014 courtesy of our extensive stats site \u2014 with some additional context. The ranking consists of players who averaged the most points in the fourth quarter ( minimum 41 games played , half the NBA season) . 1. LeBron James, 8.6 points  Being a dominant scorer over the course of a game \u2014 an average of 27.4 points \u2014 in season No. 16 is one thing. Maintaining that pace throughout the game\u2019s most important frame is another. LeBron\u2019s been a consistent force in the fourth quarter, ranking top 10 in points per game during each of the last seven seasons. His late-game numbers alone should dispel beliefs that he\u2019s slowed down or is coming off a mediocre (for him) campaign. Harden\u2019s historic season, which he described as \u201c one for the books ,\u201d included a career-high in fourth-quarter scoring. Harden unleashes every skill in his distinctive arsenal late in games, with his best fourth-quarter performance last season coming against the eventual 2019 champs. The 2018 Kia MVP also led the NBA in points scored during clutch time , the last five minutes (and overtime minutes) of games within five points. Walker earned the first All-NBA nod of his career last season, and his end-of-game performances helped achieve that. He shot 41.7 percent from the perimeter in the final period \u2014 a 6.1 percent uptick from his season average beyond the arc. From Isaiah Thomas to Kyrie Irving to now Walker, the members of Boston\u2019s point guard carousel have continued to have one thing in common: a propensity to deliver late. Much to Kemba\u2019s dismay, the reigning Kia MVP also carried his team late in games, including the fourth quarter of a Jan. 26 outing in which he outscored the entire Hornets roster. Giannis has showcased steady improvement in the late frame, raising his average from 5.5 points in 2016-17 to 6.8 points in 2017-18 and now 7.7 points in 2018-19. The cold-blooded sixth-man, who finished at the top of this list in 2017-18, knows when to put on a show. It\u2019s something about the final 12 minutes that seems to increase Williams\u2019 ability to pulverize defenses. The fourth quarter was his highest scoring period last season, and by a considerably large margin (3.2 ppg in first quarter, 5.1 ppg. in second, 4.3 in third). With Williams\u2019 immense contributions, the LA Clippers averaged the most fourth-quarter points per game (28.8) since the Denver Nuggets in the 1990-91 season (30.2), per Elias Sports Bureau. The Clippers added another upper-class closer to its rotation this summer. Fifth in total fourth-quarter points last season, George wore down defenses and scored at will when it mattered most. His timely baskets \u2014 just one element of his MVP-caliber season \u2014 were scored with remarkable 43.5\/40.0\/88.7 shooting splits. And for what it\u2019s worth: The Clippers also just added the No. 1 fourth-quarter scorer of last season\u2019s playoff run. Those final 12 minutes might feel like hours for LA\u2019s opponents. Booker, 22, is no doubt as fearless as they come, and while he\u2019s virtually the only true scorer on his team, many young players shy away from these moments. Or simply can\u2019t deliver. The Suns\u2019 sharpshooter has averaged at least six points in the fourth quarter throughout the last three seasons, well above average. Maybe teams will throw more late-game double teams at him in 2019-20? Davis\u2019 season of drama certainly overshadowed any of his on-court production. He only played in 42 fourth quarters, but averaged 6.8 points in those periods for the second consecutive season. The six-time All-Star simply knows how to create looks for himself down the stretch. Couple his late-game services with LeBron\u2019s closing capabilities, and the Lakers have some key qualities needed to win tight games in the West. In the first two seasons of Mitchell\u2019s nascent career, he\u2019s finished top-10 in this category. The poised guard shoulders a massive offensive load in Utah and carries that burden into the final period. He has 39 career games with at least 10 points in the fourth quarter alone. For context, LeBron posted 33 double-digit, fourth-quarter performances throughout his first two NBA seasons. Kobe did it 13 times, and Harden 11. Beal authored the highest-scoring season of his career with backcourt mate John Wall sidelined. Wall\u2019s injury also meant Beal would become the chief option for buckets in the fourth quarter. He answered the call, shooting at a healthy clip of 51.6 percent from the field and 40.0 percent from 3-point range in the last 12 minutes of games. Narrow it down to the last two minutes when the game is within five points and his efficiency is \u2014 impressively \u2014 just as productive (51.0, 38.1). Nearly a half-century after his graduation from the U.S. Air Force Academy, it hasn\u2019t been uncommon in recent San Antonio Spurs offseasons for Popovich to return for workouts on the wooded trails of that campus in Colorado. He\u2019d be gasping thin air found at 7,700 feet above sea level, lungs heaving, mind racing. As a student, he\u2019d go there to think. As a graduate, he\u2019s done the same. \u201cWhat you learn there is to get over yourself,\u201d said Popovich, a five-time NBA champion coach with the Spurs. \u201cIt\u2019s not about you.\u201d That is why Popovich\u2019s first stint as coach of the U.S. men\u2019s basketball team \u2014 it starts in earnest this weekend, when the Americans open their quest for a third consecutive basketball World Cup championship \u2014 has not become some sort of comeuppance tour for infamous previous attempts at gold that went awry. As such, this World Cup isn\u2019t about avenging the disappointment that Popovich still carries over getting cut from the 1972 U.S. Olympic team as a player despite having a stellar few days at tryouts for the team that lost a controversial gold-medal game to Russia. It isn\u2019t about how the 2002 world championships team that he was an assistant on finished sixth, or how the 2004 Olympic team that he assisted managed only a bronze. The Air Force Academy taught Popovich to focus on the current mission. Right now, and that\u2019s guiding the U.S. to gold in the World Cup. \u201cPop is completely locked in on this one thing,\u201d USA Basketball managing director Jerry Colangelo said. \u201cHe understands what the goal is, what we\u2019re playing for here.\u201d The Americans arrived in Shanghai on Thursday, with Popovich one of the first to greet some fans who waited at the team hotel and sign a couple dozen autographs. He took his time with each, carefully scripting the cursive, telling those who camped out on a rainy morning that there was no need to rush. His team opens play Sunday against the Czech Republic, then faces Turkey and Japan later next week in the last two group-stage games. Getting out of group play shouldn\u2019t be difficult; two of those four teams will move on to the round of 16. But a loss in an exhibition at Australia last week suggested that this U.S. team could be more than a little vulnerable against the other World Cup contenders. Popovich has been telling his team that winning the World Cup will be tough. The loss only reaffirmed what he was saying. \u201cFor a number of reasons, but ultimately the way he talks about us having these three U-S-A letters across our chest, we know what this means to him,\u201d U.S. guard Joe Harris of the Brooklyn Nets said. \u201cHe obviously has a tremendous amount of pride and respect for his country and you can feel it in how he goes about his business. This isn\u2019t something he\u2019s just doing for the hell of it.\u201d Popovich\u2019s backstory, at least the parts he wants to open up about, is well-chronicled. His undergraduate degree was in Soviet Studies. He considered a spy career and has gone through intelligence training. He\u2019s not shy about bringing up his opinions on anything, and in recent years he hasn\u2019t held back on political criticism. Economic relations right now between the U.S. and China are thorny, at best. But when Popovich arrived Thursday, donning a blue jacket with the USA Basketball red, white and blue logo, the Chinese fans who came out to greet the Americans cheered him. \u201cIt\u2019s hard for me to speculate on what this means to him,\u201d said Will Voigt, Popovich\u2019s former video coordinator in San Antonio and now the coach of the Angolan team competing in this World Cup. \u201cHe is a man of principle. And especially in this day and age in our country, with everything going on, how Team USA represents the country is very important to him. Sometimes that gets lost.\u201d Popovich hasn\u2019t shared much about his 1972 experience with his current U.S. team. He was one of about 60 players under consideration for the Olympic team that summer and shot the ball better than anyone there \u2014 he made 58 percent of his attempts \u2014 but never had a chance at getting picked for the squad. A committee was put together, plenty of politicking was happening and Popovich didn\u2019t partake in the shenanigans. So he got picked for an AAU team instead that played a series of international exhibitions. It wasn\u2019t the same. \u201cThe thing I always wanted to do was be on the Olympic team and play,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cThat was always my dream.\u201d He\u2019s been to the World Cup and Olympics as an assistant, but he\u2019s now the man in charge. He\u2019s replacing the most successful coach in U.S. history, Mike Krzyzewski, the Duke guru who led the U.S. to the last two World Cup titles and the last three Olympic golds. Popovich took a few weeks to formally accept Colangelo\u2019s invitation in 2015 to replace Krzyzewski in this cycle as national team coach for the World Cup and next year\u2019s Olympics in Tokyo. The delay probably wasn\u2019t needed. From the outset, Popovich felt compelled to jump at the chance to serve again. \u201cIt\u2019s impossible to separate it if you have been in the military,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cI\u2019ve had classmates that have fought in wars \u2014 I have not \u2014 and some of them are no longer with us. You get an appreciation for people who have sacrificed. So when you have an opportunity to do this for your country, it\u2019s impossible to say no. We\u2019ll be fine.\u201d"},{"id":32084,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/2019-fiba-world-cup-preview","date":"2019-08-29","title":"2019 FIBA World Cup Preview: The U.S., the competition and the stakes","content":" > FIBA World Cup: Team USA vs. Czech Republic (LIVE on ESPN+) SHANGHAI \u2014 The United States has won each of the last five major international tournaments on the senior level: three Olympics (2008, \u201912 and \u201916) and two World Cups (\u201910 and \u201914). Though they were undefeated throughout, finishing 42-0 across those five competitions, the U.S. has had some close calls. The 2019 FIBA World Cup could mark the toughest challenge for the United States since they finished third at the 2006 World Championship. Yet \u2013 wielding the most talent from 1-12 on any roster \u2013 the U.S. remains the favorite. But depth isn\u2019t as critical in a single-elimination scenario, nor in a game that\u2019s only 40 minutes long. The U.S. loss to Australia in an pre-tourney exhibition served as a reminder that there exists a thin line between victory and defeat, that before the Americans even compete for a medal, they could again face Australia, this time in the quarterfinals. \u201cWe were humbled a little bit,\u201d Myles Turner said. \u201cJust because you are Team USA doesn\u2019t mean you are going to win every game. Teams are looking to beat us, and we understand that now. We just have to bring it every night. There are no nights off.\u201d There are at least three rosters worth of American players who declined to play this summer or withdrew from consideration after an initial, 20-man, training-camp roster was announced in early June. In fact, after that, the U.S. added 11 more players for consideration. And to get from that group of 31 to a final, 12-man roster for the World Cup, it only had to cut two players. The other 17 either suffered injuries or withdrew. Almost four weeks into the process, after the team\u2019s first practice in Shanghai, the players were still being asked questions about the stars who decided they weren\u2019t going to play. \u201cThat doesn\u2019t matter,\u201d said point guard Kemba Walker on Thursday. \u201cIt\u2019s all about the guys who are here. We\u2019re the ones who are going to take on this challenge and do what we can to represent our country the best way we can.\u201d The \u201cguys who are here\u201d rank as solid players , but there\u2019s no question that the roster lacks star power. The U.S. Team has just two players \u2013 Jaylen Brown and Jayson Tatum \u2013 who were drafted in the top five; every other USA roster with NBA players since 1992 has had at least four top-five picks. Just one player \u2013 Kemba Walker \u2013 has ever made an All-NBA team; he placed on the Third Team last season. The only players with senior-level, national-team experience are Mason Plumlee and Harrison Barnes, who had minor roles on the 2014 and 2016 teams, respectively. But experience isn\u2019t as important as the ability to just get buckets when they\u2019re needed. The U.S. has Walker, Tatum and Donovan Mitchell for that task, but those guys are a step below Kevin Durant (who has scored at least 28 points in each of the three gold-medal games in which he\u2019s played), Kyrie Irving (26 in the 2014 gold-medal game) and James Harden (23 in that same 2014 game) in that regard. Though the Australia outcome belies it, the U.S. certainly has the ability to be the best defensive team in the tournament. \u201cThat\u2019s going to be our ticket,\u201d Walker said earlier in training. \u201cThat\u2019s going to be what gets us over the hump. Defensively, we just have to be monsters. We have to.\u201d The U.S. will begin play in Group E, playing games in Shanghai against the Czech Republic (Sept. 1), Turkey (Sept. 3) and Japan (Sept. 5). The top two teams from that pool will advance to the second round, where they will join with the top two teams from Group F (Brazil, Greece, Montenegro and New Zealand) to form Group K in Shenzhen. One of those four games (the two teams from Group E will play one game apiece against the two games from Group F) will very likely feature the U.S. facing NBA MVP Giannis Antetokounmpo and Greece. That probably won\u2019t be an elimination game, but only two teams from Group K will advance to the quarterfinals. Eight groups of four (A-H) turn into four groups of four (I-L), and from those four groups, we get eight teams for the single-elimination tournament that begins September 10 in Dongguan and Shanghai. The groups aren\u2019t all that balanced. You could argue that there are three teams in Group H (Australia, Canada and Lithuania) better than any team in Group A. Argentina isn\u2019t nearly the same team it was several years ago, but it\u2019s likely the best team in Groups A\/B\/I. The two teams that emerge from Group H, meanwhile, will have to compete with France out of Group G for two of the spots in the quarterfinals. Assuming that the U.S. advances out of Group K, its quarterfinal opponent will come from that Australia-France-Lithuania mix. So the Americans could have an elimination-game against a medal-worthy opponent right away. If the favorite isn\u2019t the United States, it\u2019s Serbia, which went 10-0 in its exhibition slate , beating France, Greece, Italy (twice), Lithuania (twice) and Turkey. The Serbs were the silver medalists at the 2014 World Cup and the 2016 Olympics, and they now have an improved and more mature Nikola Jokic (though the tournament won\u2019t be the same without the injured Milos Teodosic). Jokic is Exhibit A of how most of the top talent on other teams is on the frontline. France has Rudy Gobert, Australia has Aron Baynes and Andrew Bogut, Spain has Marc Gasol, and Lithuania has both Domantas Sabonis and Jonas Valanciunas. Seven teams from the World Cup will qualify for next year\u2019s Olympics in Tokyo, but they\u2019re not necessarily the top seven finishers. The teams that will qualify for the Olympics are: As the host, Japan is automatically qualified for the Olympics. The other four teams in the 12-team Olympic field will come from qualifying tournaments that take place early next summer. That\u2019s not too fair to Europe, which accounts for 12 of the 32 (and probably six of the top eight) teams in the World Cup field. But that\u2019s the way it works. So, even if the U.S. were to lose in the knockout rounds, it will almost surely qualify for the Olympics, because it probably won\u2019t finish lower than two other teams from the Americas. As noted above, Argentina has a very good chance of reaching the quarterfinals, but it will be difficult for any of the other five teams from the Americas \u2013 Brazil, Canada, the Dominican Republic, Puerto Rico and Venezuela \u2013 to break through. The Americans aren\u2019t here just to qualify for the Olympics, though. Ten new players on the roster means 10 guys who have never won gold. A standard has been set and a loss, no matter how many players declined to be here, would be a huge disappointment. * * * John Schuhmann is a senior stats analyst for NBA.com. An all-night flight from Sydney to Shanghai that landed early Thursday brought the two-time defending World Cup champion Americans to China\u2019s most-populous city, where they\u2019ll play three first round games starting Sunday. It took more than 10 hours of flying time, then another two-plus hours for the team to clear customs and finally reach its hotel. From there, a few hours of relaxing awaited before an afternoon practice. \u201cThe challenges begin,\u201d U.S. coach Gregg Popovich said. A handful of fans waited outside the team hotel on a rainy morning, getting there a couple hours before the buses from the airport pulled in just with the hope of grabbing a few autographs. Some players obliged, as did Popovich \u2014 who used a gold marker to carefully sign his name on an array of photos, sneakers and basketballs. Players said finally getting to China brought a different feel. \u201cIt\u2019s kicked in,\u201d U.S. guard Kemba Walker of the Boston Celtics said after practice. \u201cThe next game we play, it\u2019s the real thing. We\u2019re focused, we\u2019re locked in and we\u2019re ready to play.\u201d It\u2019s not like there hasn\u2019t been challenges already. Just consider the travel itineraries for the U.S. to this point. The flights from Los Angeles to Melbourne, then Melbourne to Sydney and now Sydney to Shanghai add up to nearly 30 hours and 14,000 miles in the air. If the U.S. makes the medal round, there\u2019ll be about another 2,500 miles of travel within China. Add the return flight to the U.S. after the tournament, and the trip\u2019s total will easily exceed 22,000 miles \u2014 more than half a regular season\u2019s worth of travel for most NBA teams. All that flying comes in the span of basically a month. The team will introduce a modern take on the fan-favorite black uniform that originally debuted during the 1994-95 season when the Cavs returned to downtown Cleveland to play in the brand-new Gund Arena after two decades of playing more than 20 miles away at the Coliseum in Richfield, Ohio. The team\u2019s much-anticipated homecoming introduced a fresh new identity for the Cavs that featured a roster that included Mark Price, John \u201cHot Rod\u201d Williams, Chris Mills, Bobby Phills, Tyrone Hill and Terrell Brandon under head coach Mike Fratello, and ushered in a new era of Cavaliers basketball in the heart of their namesake city. \u201cThese retro uniforms spark special memories and feelings for our fans and the organization alike. Each \u201cEra Night\u201d will feature exclusive giveaways, unique content and activities, in-game moments and more\u2014all to give fans the opportunity to relive and experience the journey of the Cavaliers over the last 50 seasons. The Cavaliers will wear the Classic Edition uniform during eight games throughout the 2019-20 season, including the Cavs home opener. Designed in collaboration with Nike, the Classic Edition is a one-year alternate uniform and joins the Icon (wine), Association (white), City (to be announced at a later date) and Statement (black) uniforms as one of five uniforms in the Cavs 2019-20 season collection. The front of the black shell features CLEVELAND in an orange and black inline typeface that is slanted upwards across the chest. The black shorts feature the Cavs logo from 1994-2003 and a blue splash that stretches from the bottom of the right leg to the top of the left leg. He didn\u2019t get much of one this year. There\u2019s a very good reason for that \u2014 a most unusual and, he thinks, worthwhile opportunity. After helping the Toronto Raptors win the NBA championship in June, Gasol is now looking to lead Spain to a World Cup title in September. And although the 7-foot-1 veteran center\u2019s body may have preferred some more downtime before the grind of another season begins, Gasol could not pass up this chance. \u201cIt\u2019s a special group of guys,\u201d Gasol said. \u201cIt\u2019s always special when you put on this jersey. And I couldn\u2019t leave them hanging. That\u2019s what my heart told me and that\u2019s what it keeps telling me.\u201d Gasol was on the team that won the World Cup \u2014 then called the world championship \u2014 for Spain in 2006, rolling past a Greece team that had just beaten the United States in the tournament semifinals. He helped Spain win silver medals at the 2008 and 2012 Olympics, losing both times in the title game to the U.S. He\u2019s the oldest player on a very seasoned team that will play for Spain in this World Cup. Out of the 12 on the final roster for coach Sergio Scariolo, eight have celebrated their 30th birthdays already. But it\u2019s also clear that Gasol, even on a roster featuring the likes of Phoenix\u2019s Ricky Rubio and Real Madrid standout Sergio Llull, is the leader of the bunch. \u201cIt was probably a key move for us, one of the important ones, the most important one,\u201d Scariolo said. \u201cWe need somebody to be the guy who you can give the ball in the tough moments, not necessarily for the shot but to make a good play \u2014 whether it\u2019s to create a shot for a teammate, to take a shot himself, to draw a foul and be a solid free throw shooter. He\u2019s extremely important and the rest of the players respect him a lot.\u201d That respect was there before Toronto topped Golden State in six games for the NBA title. But the ring Gasol will be getting on opening night certainly adds to his legacy. Among players born outside the United States, Gasol is one of only seven \u2014 a list that also includes his older brother Pau Gasol, who would have played in this World Cup had he not gotten injured last season \u2014 to have amassed more than 11,000 points, 6,000 rebounds and 2,700 assists at the NBA level. And when the Raptors added him in a trade last February, their entire makeup seemed to change. \u201cI think we started passing the ball, our assists started going way up, we became the No. 1 3-point shooting team in the league because of the extra passes and the contagious passing,\u201d said Raptors coach Nick Nurse, who is coaching Canada at the World Cup. \u201cAnd our team\u2019s sense of who they thought they could become went up.\u201d The same could ring true for Spain. The U.S. has won the last two World Cups, though a third consecutive gold in the event \u2014 something that no nation has ever accomplished \u2014 hardly seems guaranteed. Spain lost to the Americans by nine in an exhibition earlier this month in Anaheim, California, a game where neither side was exactly in tournament form. >> Every NBA Players In FIBA World Cup Spain should have little, if any, trouble getting through its group phase: It faces Iran, Tunisia and the Dominican Republic in its first three games at Guangzhou, China starting on Friday. The top two teams will advance to the second round. Those first three games will likely become mere tune-ups for Gasol and the Spainards, as they get ready for the bigger matchups later in the tournament. \u201cThe teams that are in the past, they\u2019re in the past,\u201d Gasol said. \u201cWhat matters is the guys who are playing today and their talent and their qualities.\u201d There has been minimal rest for Gasol this summer. Exhibit A: 19 turnovers in the team\u2019s 84-68 exhibition win over Canada on Monday. When it opens the World Cup with a game against the Czech Republic on Sunday, the U.S. will have had just 15 practices and five exhibition games to prepare. And the final, 12-man roster has only been together and healthy for two of those games. With a roster that\u2019s light on stars yet heavy on good players from good teams, it takes time to figure out a rotation. Five games might not be enough, and it\u2019s clear that the entire exhibition slate has been an experiment in regard to lineups. Head coach Gregg Popovich used five different starting lineups in the five games, with 10 different players starting at least one game. With different starting lineups, there were different second units each night. As a result, only two five-man units played at least 10 minutes over the five games, and only five lineups played in more than one game together. In the exhibition finale (against Canada on Monday), the U.S. didn\u2019t use a single lineup that had played in any of the four previous games. So there\u2019s not much to be gleaned from the numbers for any five-man unit. It\u2019s all small sample sizes. Of course, small sample sizes are all you get with the national team. The U.S. will play just five more games before they reach the elimination rounds of the World Cup. And at that point, one bad stretch could end the United States\u2019 run atop the basketball world. The Americans have won five straight major tournaments, but a third straight World Championship may be the toughest task of that run. The loss to Australia didn\u2019t count, but was the first defeat for an American team comprised of all NBA players since the semifinals of the 2006 World Championship. While there\u2019s not much to be learned from the 103 different lineups that the Senior Team used over the five exhibition games (including one against the U.S. Select Team), the overall data could tell us a few things \u2026 Donovan Mitchell and Kemba Walker were the U.S. Team\u2019s second most-used two-man combination in the exhibition games, having played a little more than 69 minutes together. But De\u2019Aaron Fox\u2019s decision (prior to the team\u2019s departure for Australia) to withdraw has left the U.S. with just three primary ball-handlers, and the third of those \u2014 Derrick White \u2014 has been the 11th man in the rotation. The win over Canada featured Popovich\u2019s tightest rotation. The five starters were back on the floor just a minute and a half into the second quarter, White didn\u2019t play until late in the first half, and Brook Lopez didn\u2019t play until midway through the third quarter. But with Mitchell and Walker starting together, there were still some minutes with neither of them (nor White) on the floor. The second-unit backcourt was Marcus Smart and Joe Harris, neither of whom has nearly the same ability to break down a defense as Mitchell or Walker. And with Smart on the floor without Mitchell, Walker or White (over the last two exhibition games), the U.S. scored just 13 points on 18 possessions. The first 2:47 of the second quarter of the U.S. Team\u2019s loss to Australia on Saturday was particularly ugly. The Americans scored just two points on five possessions, with those two points coming when Australia fouled Smart on a late-clock, off-balance 3-pointer. That\u2019s a small sample size and the Smart-led offense could certainly improve going forward, but the U.S. might be better off staggering the minutes of Mitchell and Walker so that one of the two is on the floor at all times. The offense has actually been more efficient with only one *ball-handler on the floor than it has been with two. * Counting Fox, Mitchell, Walker and White as ball-handlers. If Kyle Kuzma didn\u2019t suffer an ankle injury before the loss to Australia, it would have been interesting to see if Popovich and USA Basketball managing director Jerry Colangelo kept all three centers on the roster. Either way, Myles Turner has clearly established himself as the starting center. Turner not only shot 71 percent over the five exhibition games, he grabbed a team-best 12.7 rebounds per 30 minutes, and led the team in both total plus-minus (plus-48) and on-court NetRtg, with the U.S. outscoring its opponents by 27.4 points per 100 possessions in his 83 minutes on the floor. Mason Plumlee has also been an integral part of the rotation. Though Plumlee took just four shots (and two free throws) in 49 total minutes over the five exhibition games, the U.S. scored 122 points per 100 possessions with him on the floor. That was the best on-court OffRtg mark among the players on the final roster. With Turner and Plumlee getting the bulk of the playing time at center, Brook Lopez has played just 17 minutes over the last three games. He averaged 7.9 3-point attempts per 36 minutes with the Bucks last season, but attempted just four 3s in 37 total minutes, and he was the only player on the final roster that had a negative plus-minus (minus-16) over the exhibition slate. The U.S. has also played a little less than 21 minutes with none of the three centers on the floor. In fact, Popovich went small for most of the fourth quarter of his team\u2019s loss to Australia on Saturday. The small-ball defense allowed 13 points on 11 possessions down the stretch in the loss, but has been strong otherwise. Take away that fourth quarter on Saturday and small-ball lineups allowed just 28 points in 34 possessions. Small ball, small sample. While Walker, Mitchell and Turner appear to be sure things to start, the starting forward spots could still be wide open. The U.S. started four different combinations at the three and four in the five exhibition games, with Harrison Barnes and Khris Middleton being the only pair of forwards that started more than one game together. Jaylen Brown and Jayson Tatum didn\u2019t start any games together, but played more minutes together (40) than any pair of forwards. And, within the group of four forwards, that was Tatum\u2019s most successful pairing. The U.S. outscored its opponents by 20 points per 100 possessions with the two young Celtics on the floor together, but was outscored by 16 per 100 in 49 total minutes with Tatum on the floor with either Barnes or Middleton. Joe Harris also got one start at the three and played 22 minutes total alongside both Walker and Mitchell. Harris was only able to get 10 3-pointers up in his 95 minutes (six of his teammates attempted more 3s per minute), but he rebounded well for his position and the U.S. allowed less than 95 points per 100 possessions with him on the floor. Without great chemistry or the one-on-one stars that can get buckets by themselves, defense is more important than its ever been. While there were some ugly offensive stretches in the loss to Australia, it was on defense where the numbers were far worse than they were in their four exhibition wins. * * * John Schuhmann is a staff writer for NBA.com. The eight-time All-Star center and 15-year NBA veteran is the Lakers\u2019 improbable choice to fill the sudden roster vacancy created by DeMarcus Cousins\u2019 knee injury. Howard spent one memorable season with the Lakers in 2012-13 after joining the club with Steve Nash in Los Angeles\u2019 high-risk attempt to create an immediate championship contender. While he led the NBA in rebounding and valiantly played through injuries, Howard also clashed with Kobe Bryant and subsequently spurned Los Angeles as a free agent after the Lakers lost in the first round of the playoffs. He bounced to six franchises after his departure, while the Lakers haven\u2019t made the NBA postseason in those ensuing six seasons. Howard has been aggressively booed at Staples Center ever since he took significantly less money than the Lakers offered him and joined the Houston Rockets instead. Howard appeared in nine games last season after joining Washington, but he hasn\u2019t played since November after undergoing spinal surgery. When healthy with the Charlotte Hornets in 2017-18, Howard averaged 16.6 points and 12.5 rebounds per game. The 33-year-old Howard will take over the role expected to be filled by Cousins, who tore his knee ligament shortly after signing with the Lakers last month. Cousins could miss the entire upcoming season, so Howard will team with JaVale McGee and Anthony Davis to play center for Los Angeles. With career averages of 17.4 points, 12.7 rebounds and 2.0 blocked shots per game, Howard is undeniably one of the greatest big men of his generation. But he has been criticized throughout his career for his attitude and locker room presence, and he made few fans in Los Angeles. Howard\u2019s impending return to LA over the past week generated conflicting feelings among Lakers fans online, but Howard clearly persuaded the Lakers he can be a strong supporting player and a good teammate when he worked out for the club. The Lakers had locker room upheaval last season, but it was caused mostly by developments outside the room \u2014 particularly the front office\u2019s ultimately fruitless pursuit of Davis in a midseason trade. LeBron James and Rajon Rondo emerged as leaders in their first season with the club, and they\u2019ll again be in charge of a roster with several major changes. The Lakers waived forward Aric Holman to create a roster spot for Howard. The Athletic\u2019s Shams Charania reports that Howard will wear No. 39 this season. An eight-time NBA All-Star and the 2004 first overall draft pick, Howard appeared in nine games (all starts) with the Wizards last season, where he averaged 12.8 points and 9.2 rebounds in 25.6 minutes. He returns to Los Angeles after posting 17.1 points and a league-best 12.4 rebounds in 2012-13, his lone season with the team. Howard is a three-time Defensive Player of the Year \u2013 winning the award in consecutive seasons from 2009-11 \u2013 and has led the league in rebounds five times (2007-10, \u201911-13), blocks twice (2008-10) and field goal percentage once (2009-10). The Bob Cousy Award, given to the country\u2019s best point guard in men\u2019s college basketball, is named for him. He is a member of the Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame and played a pivotal role in founding the NBA Player\u2019s Association. After hanging up his No. 14 jersey, the 13-time NBA All-Star went on to coach basketball at Boston College. \u201cThis acknowledgment allows me to complete my life circle,\u201d Cousy said during the Oval Office awards ceremony. \u201cI can stop chasing a bouncing ball. The Presidential Medal of Freedom allows me to reach a level of acceptance in our society I never once ever dreamed of.\u201d Trump spoke of Cousy\u2019s childhood during the Great Depression and discovering his talent for basketball at a young age. The president said Cousy never forgot his first mentor\u2019s advice to never be predictable, and jokingly added: \u201cHey, I\u2019ve heard that lesson, too.\u201d The president recognized Cousy\u2019s achievements on and off the court, lauding his support for underprivileged young athletes and speaking out against racism. Cousy, who is white, ardently supported his black teammates who faced discrimination during the civil rights movement. Still, Cousy lamented in Gary Pomerantz\u2019s biography \u201cThe Last Pass: Cousy, Russell, the Celtics, and What Matters in the End,\u201d that he didn\u2019t do more for his black teammates, including 2011 Medal of Freedom recipient Bill Russell. The Medal of Freedom, the nation\u2019s highest civilian honor, celebrates individuals for their \u201cespecially meritorious contribution to the security or national interests of the U.S., to world peace, or to cultural or other significant public or private endeavors.\u201d Trump credited West Virginia Sen. Joe Manchin for suggesting the medal be given to Cousy. Cousy is the second Medal of Freedom recipient this year. Trump presented the award to golfer Tiger Woods in May. Cousy is the 10th honoree under Trump, who is Cousy\u2019s candidate of choice in the 2020 presidential election. In a recent interview with NBA.com , Cousy described himself as politically moderate. He said that although he disagrees with some of the president\u2019s actions, he plans to vote for Trump next year. During the award ceremony, Cousy said the medal was made all the more special because it had been presented by the \u201cmost extraordinary\u201d president in his lifetime. \u201cI know in your world, you\u2019re well on your way to making America great again,\u201d Cousy told the president. \u201cIn my world, it\u2019s been great for 91 years. The 2019-20 season marks the 25th anniversary of the debut of the purple uniforms during the 1994-95 season. \u201cAfter having had teal and white Classic Edition uniforms the last two seasons, it is only right that we complete the set with the purple one this year,\u201d said Hornets President & Vice Chairman Fred Whitfield. \u201cWith this season being the 25th anniversary of the purple uniform\u2019s introduction in 1994, this is the perfect time to bring back a Classic Edition version.\u201d The Hornets are scheduled to wear the purple Classic Edition uniforms for five home games this season \u2013 Saturday, November 9, against the New Orleans Pelicans; Friday, December 27, against the Oklahoma City Thunder; Saturday, February 22, against the Brooklyn Nets; Saturday, March 7, against the Houston Rockets; and Saturday, March 28, against the Los Angeles Clippers. Based on the uniform worn during the Hornets\u2019 first decade, the purple Classic Edition jersey includes the familiar crossover v-neck and multi-colored pinstripes in light blue, royal blue, green and teal. The shorts feature the classic Hornets logo on the waist and the same white, purple and teal trim as the original.  The original purple uniform was worn during some of the most memorable seasons in franchise history. In 1994-95, the Hornets won 50 games for the first time and had two All-Stars in the same season for the only time ever with Larry Johnson and Alonzo Mourning. Two years later, the 1996-97 Hornets had the best season in team history, going 54-28 as Glen Rice set a multitude of franchise single-season records. Along with being named MVP of the NBA All-Star Game, Rice (Second Team) and Anthony Mason (Third Team) gave the Hornets multiple All-NBA selections in a season for the only time. Like the rest of the team\u2019s uniforms, the purple Classic Edition features the logos of Nike\u2019s Jordan Brand on the right chest and partner LendingTree on the left chest. The Official Loan Shopping Partner of the Charlotte Hornets, LendingTree will have its logo on each of the team\u2019s jerseys for the third consecutive season. As part of a robust sponsorship package, the company is also the entitlement partner for the Hornets App and the Hornets Hoops youth basketball program. The purple Classic Edition jersey is expected to be available at retail after the start of the regular season. It\u2019s reasonable to assume that Popovich and his coaching staff and the USA Basketball brass need every minute they can muster to separate the final two members of the group from the back to carve out the most cohesive group they can for the competition. Parker will become the 10th player in Spurs franchise history to have his number raised to the rafters, joining Bruce Bowen (12), Tim Duncan (21), Sean Elliott (32), George Gervin (44), Manu Ginobili (20), Avery Johnson (6), Johnny Moore (00), David Robinson (50) and James Silas (13). In 17 seasons in San Antonio, Parker helped the Silver and Black capture four NBA championships and was named the 2007 NBA Finals MVP, becoming the first European Finals MVP in history. The point guard from France was a four-time All-NBA performer (2009, 2012, 2013, 2014) and a six-time NBA All-Star (2006, 2007, 2009, 2012, 2013, 2014) with the Spurs. Originally selected by San Antonio with the 28th overall pick in the first round of the 2001 NBA Draft, Parker is the Spurs NBA leader in assists (6,829), while ranking second in games played (1,198), fourth in points (18,943) and steals (1,032), fifth in free throws made (3,309) and sixth in rebounds (3,313). Parker is one of five players in NBA history to post at least 19,000 points and 7,000 assists, along with Oscar Robertson, John Stockton, Gary Payton and LeBron James. He played in a total of 1,254 career games in 18 seasons with the Spurs and Charlotte Hornets, averaging 15.5 points, 5.6 assists and 2.7 rebounds in 30.5 minutes. Parker finished his career seventh in NBA history with 892 wins. Appearing in a total of 226 postseason contests with the Spurs, sixth most all-time, Parker averaged 17.9 points, 5.1 assists and 2.9 rebounds in 34.3 minutes. In NBA Playoffs history, Parker ranks fifth all-time in assists (1,143) and ninth in points (4,045). Parker and fellow Spurs jersey retirees Tim Duncan and Manu Ginobili recorded 126 postseason victories together, which are the most wins by any trio in NBA history. Parker is one of four players in league history to record 4,000 points and 1,000 assists in the NBA Playoffs, along with Michael Jordan, Kobe Bryant and LeBron James. He was one of 66 players who tried out for the 1972 Olympic team when the trials were held at his alma mater, the Air Force Academy. It was a team Popovich, and plenty of others, thought he should have been on. But he was cut. \u201cI got screwed,\u201d Popovich said, the topic striking an obvious nerve all these years later. \u201cI was devastated when I didn\u2019t make it, as anybody would be.\u201d Popovich was put on an alternate team that he said went on a tour to Brazil and Argentina and partied \u201ctheir [expletive] off.\u201d \u201cI don\u2019t even know, we probably lost every game,\u201d he said. \u201cAnd that\u2019s the truth. But I was young and foolish and it wasn\u2019t the real team and we were down there for kicks or whatever. And we did that.\u201d Back then a committee decided who made the team, a much more political process than what happens today. But the memories of that time, and particularly the infamous Gold medal game when the U.S. Team lost in a hugely controversial finish to the Soviet Union team, will never fade. \u201cIn addition to the ridiculous situation at the end of that game, I\u2019ll always remember Doug Collins,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cThe two most pressurized and important free throws I\u2019ve ever seen anybody shoot, and I don\u2019t care about NBA championships or anything else. To have to make those two free throws that he made, at his age, just incredible. It still gives me goose bumps every time I think about him having to have the courage to step up and do that. That\u2019s the big thing for me.\u201d http:\/\/draft De\u2019Aaron Fox said he takes pride in being one several members of the NBA\u2019s 2017 Draft class on display this summer on both the Senior Team and the Select Team that has worked out with and against the squad that will represent the program in China. \u201cI think it\u2019s great to have guys you come into the league with here as well,\u201d Fox said. \u201cIt\u2019s definitely something you\u2019ll talk about years now down the road. And I think it says the league is in good hands with so many hard-working guys here, not to mention other talented guys who could be here as well. It just speaks to how competitive the league is and how young it is right now.\u201d Fox, Jayson Tatum, Donovan Mitchell, Kyle Kuzma and Derrick White have all made it to the final phase of the selection process. They\u2019re all packed for China, though it won\u2019t be known until Friday night\u2019s game if they all will make the trip.  Either way, Tucker said, you can\u2019t help but he impressed with the array of young talent that has been on display. \u201cHonestly, all of these guys are better than I realized,\u201d Tucker said. \u201cPlaying against people twice a year or whatever is one thing. But when you get here and you\u2019re working out together every day and you see these guys work, all of these young guys. De\u2019Aaron Fox is amazing. He\u2019s way better than I thought he was, and not saying that I didn\u2019t think he was good. But he\u2019s really, really good. \u201cAnd I play Donovan all the time in Utah and I know he\u2019s really good. But out here he\u2019s been great. Jayson Tatum is great. All these guys, top to bottom, are really, really good, and they\u2019re going to be great in their individual careers.\u201d The big winner in a FIBA summer, according to Popovich, are the teams these players \u2014 and players from every country competing \u2014 go back to after the competition is over. It\u2019s a shot of energy to the global basketball ecosystem, he said, that certainly works for the NBA. \u201cBasketball has become so international, with so many great players everywhere, and everyone benefits,\u201d Popovich said. \u201cWhen they get back to their NBA teams, most everybody is probably a better player. They\u2019ve had more experiences and all the competitiveness they had to exhibit in the tournament carries over.\u201d * * * Sekou Smith is a veteran NBA reporter and NBA TV analyst.
